Current Affairs Commentary

Eradicating National Illiteracy 14

— Dou

Since human affairs become increasingly complex and writing becomes increasingly important, whether to express ideas internally or to understand knowledge externally, almost all rely on it for communication. Today, as we pool national strength to seek overall development, it is essential to have a universal and profound influence. Observing the movement to promote wisdom within the country, we can only be somewhat optimistic in very limited cities. Most rural and remote areas are filled with ignorant people who do not understand the Qin and Han dynasties, let alone the Wei and Jin dynasties. If we want to popularize education and give everyone a drive, how can we succeed? I recently heard that the Ministry of Education has made a decision to eradicate national illiteracy and is currently drafting measures to promote mass education in the responsible department, aiming to eliminate 200 million illiterate people within six years, establish a foundation for education, and promote social progress. This sound in the empty mountains is cause for excitement.

In recent years, the authorities have also been working hard on education. They have put their heart and soul into compulsory education, used radio broadcasting for propaganda, and simultaneously planned for both free education and special education, which were widely promoted for a time. However, due to frequent disasters and disturbances in recent years, they have not been able to achieve significant results. Now, with the call for a six-year plan, we see the authorities' determination to eradicate illiteracy. With my limited ability, I dare to offer a humble suggestion.

Eradicating illiteracy is not easy to achieve quickly, given the vast area of our country and the prevalence of illiteracy. If the authorities are determined and can formulate a detailed plan, there should be no worries about the implementation process. The lack of talent is not a problem; while illiterate people are everywhere in the country today, there is also a significant surplus of wandering and displaced intellectuals. We should know that there are many knowledgeable people in the unemployment environment, either wandering due to unfavorable circumstances or being rejected due to a lack of support. There are also those who were originally teachers but were dismissed due to a lack of qualifications or were eliminated due to overly strict screening. We can be inclusive and recruit them all, provide them with the necessary training, and offer them reasonable financial assistance. We can then send them to the countryside to promote the work of eradicating illiteracy. As for the materials used, we should consider the situation and specially compile them, striving to adapt them to the needs of the rural people and focusing on being able to attract their interest. Furthermore, we should assign those with eloquence and quick wit among the staff to be responsible for public speaking, and those with skilled writing to be responsible for writing. Local educational institutions should supervise the progress at all times, assess the results, and impose rewards and punishments accordingly. In this way, on the one hand, we can provide intellectual relief, and on the other hand, we can also alleviate occupational hunger. Those who are concerned should not dismiss these words as irrelevant.

What must be done in conjunction with this is to increase the number of newspapers and posters and create more pictorial propaganda. We can instruct the staff to explain their meaning in simple terms. At the same time, we can consult with those who perform low-level entertainment arts, such as storytellers, to help instill knowledge. We can distribute simple explanations of the text when they tell stories to induce a desire for knowledge, which may have considerable effects. The main thing is that things depend on people, and with determination, we can achieve success. Whether we can succeed in eradicating illiteracy depends on the authorities' determination.

Statistics on Opium Smokers in Wuhan 15

(Hankou) Since the Wuhan Public Security Bureau took over the ban on opium smoking last July, due to the lack of cooperation between the special zone and the French concessions, only 11,434 opium smokers have been registered and 2,012 opium smokers have been persuaded to quit so far. Furthermore, due to the difficulty in funding for only one municipal hospital as a smoking cessation institution, it is impossible to accommodate opium smokers as much as possible. Now, a part of the prison building has been borrowed from the Second Prison, which can accommodate 500 people. It is reported that the Public Security Bureau, in order to make the reporting of opium smokers more thorough, will add female staff to assist in strict investigations to prevent private smoking. (Central News Agency dispatch of the 3rd)

National Government Promulgates Provisional Regulations for the Suppression of Opium and Punishment of Offenders 16

And Announces Regulations for the Organization of Anti-Opium Associations at All Levels

(Nanjing) The National Government promulgated the Provisional Regulations for the Suppression of Opium and Punishment of Offenders on the 3rd. The original text is as follows:

Article 1: These regulations are based on item 4 of the resolution of the 459th meeting of the Central Political Committee.

Article 2: In these regulations, "opium" refers to opium, poppies, and poppy seeds.

Article 3: Those who plant poppies with the intention of manufacturing opium shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than ten years.

Article 4: Those who gather a crowd to resist the eradication of opium seedlings shall be punished as follows: (1) The instigators or those in command on the scene shall be sentenced to death or life imprisonment. (2) The remaining members shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years.

Article 5: Those who transport, sell, or possess opium with the intention of selling it shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for not less than five years and may also be fined not more than 3,000 yuan. Those whose quantity is 500 taels or more shall be sentenced to death. Those who transport, sell, or possess poppy seeds with the intention of selling them shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years and may also be fined not more than 1,000 yuan. Those who import opium or poppy seeds from foreign countries shall be sentenced to death, life imprisonment, or imprisonment for not less than ten years and may also be fined not more than 5,000 yuan. The same applies to those who export them to foreign countries.

Article 6: Those who, with the intention of making a profit, establish a place to provide opium and opium paraphernalia for others to smoke shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for not less than five years and may also be fined not more than 3,000 yuan.

Article 7: Those who use a limited-time opium cessation license to provide opium for others to smoke for profit shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than seven years and may also be fined not more than 1,000 yuan.

Article 8: Those who smoke opium shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than six months and not more than two years and may also be fined not more than 300 yuan. Those who are addicted shall also be ordered to undergo medical treatment within a limited time to break the addiction. Those who voluntarily submit to treatment and break the addiction and then commit the aforementioned crime again shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than one year and not more than three years and may also be fined not more than 500 yuan. Those who are addicted shall still be ordered to undergo medical treatment within a limited time to break the addiction. Those who, after being ordered to break the addiction, commit the crime in the first paragraph again shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than three years and not more than ten years and may also be fined not more than 1,000 yuan. Those who are addicted shall still be ordered to undergo medical treatment within a limited time to break the addiction. Those who commit the offense for a third time shall be sentenced to death. School teachers, staff, and students who commit any of the aforementioned three crimes shall be punished with the maximum penalty for each crime.

Article 9: Those who help others commit the crimes in Articles 3, 5, and 6 of these regulations shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than seven years. Those who help others commit the crime in Article 6 shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than three years, regardless of whether the principal offender is a first-time offender or a repeat offender.

Article 10: Those who frame or fabricate evidence to falsely accuse others of committing the crimes in the various articles of these regulations shall be punished with the penalty for each article. The same applies to witnesses who intentionally make false statements or reports with the intention of harming the defendant suspected of committing the crimes in the various articles of these regulations. Those who confess to committing the aforementioned two crimes before the judgment in the case is finalized may have their penalty reduced or waived.

Article 11: Public officials who commit the crimes in Articles 3 to 6 of these regulations shall be sentenced to death. Those who commit the crimes in Articles 8 to 10 shall be punished with the maximum penalty for each article.

Article 12: Public officials who use their authority to force others to commit the crime in Article 3 of these regulations shall be sentenced to death.

Article 13: Public officials who harbor or demand, promise, or accept bribes and connive with others to commit the crimes in Articles 3 to 6 of these regulations shall be sentenced to death. The same applies to public officials who steal, exchange, or conceal seized opium, embezzle anti-opium fines, or intentionally allow offenders of the various articles of these regulations to escape. Public officials who harbor or demand, promise, or accept bribes and connive with others to commit the crimes in Articles 7 to 9 of these regulations shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not less than seven years. The bribes received by those who commit the crimes in paragraphs 1 and 3 of this article shall be confiscated. If all or part of the bribes cannot be confiscated, their value shall be recovered.

Article 14: Those who manufacture, transport, sell, or possess instruments exclusively for smoking opium with the intention of selling them shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than three years, detention, or a fine of not more than 1,000 yuan.

Article 15: Attempted offenses of Articles 3 to 6, 10, 12 to 14 of these regulations shall be punished.

Article 16: Those who knowingly possess opium or instruments exclusively for smoking opium shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than 500 yuan.

Article 17: The opium or instruments exclusively for manufacturing or smoking opium involved in the crimes of the various articles of these regulations shall be confiscated.

Article 18: Those who are sentenced to imprisonment for not less than six months for committing the crimes in the various articles of these regulations shall be deprived of their civil rights for not less than one year and not more than ten years.

Article 19: Those who commit the crimes in Articles 3, 5, and 6 of these regulations may have all or part of their property confiscated. The execution of the confiscation of property shall be subject to the provisions of the Civil Procedure Execution Rules and the Supplementary Civil Execution Measures.

Article 20: The penal provisions of the anti-opium laws and regulations promulgated by the Chairman's Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission and the various provinces and cities before the implementation of these regulations shall become invalid on the date of implementation of these regulations, except for those that have been approved to continue to apply. If the law at the time of judgment has changed, the law at the time of the act shall apply.

Article 21: The death penalty may be executed by shooting.

Article 22: If the various provinces and regions have other regulations due to the phased eradication over the years, those regulations shall prevail.

Article 23: Matters not provided for in these regulations shall be subject to the provisions of other laws and regulations.

Article 24: Those who commit the crimes in the various articles of these regulations shall be tried by the organ with military judicial authority designated by the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission concurrently serving as the Director-General of Anti-Opium, or the local governments at all levels may be entrusted to try them on his behalf. The decisions made in accordance with the provisions of the preceding paragraph shall not be executed unless they have been submitted to the Chairman and Director-General of Anti-Opium for approval, except as handled in accordance with the Provisional Measures for the Supreme Military Organs of the Various Provinces to Review Military Judicial Cases on behalf of the Central Government.

Article 25: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

(Nanjing) The National Government issued an order on the 3rd, promulgating the Regulations for the Organization of the Anti-Opium Director-General's Office of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government and the Regulations for the Organization of Anti-Opium Committees of the various provinces, cities, and counties. This order is hereby issued. The Regulations for the Organization of the Anti-Opium Director-General's Office consist of nineteen articles. The main points are as follows: The Office shall have a number of members, who shall be employed or appointed by the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission concurrently serving as the Director-General of Anti-Opium from among impartial individuals with a passion for the cause from the various provinces and cities, and three members shall be designated as standing committee members. The Office shall be specially entrusted by the concurrent Director-General to handle matters within the authority of the Director-General. All matters concerning the handling of anti-opium and anti-drug affairs and matters of rewards and punishments by the governments of the various provinces and cities and the anti-opium committees of the various provinces and cities shall be supervised, urged, and reviewed by the Office. The various committees may make suggestions at any time regarding the promotion of anti-opium and anti-drug efforts and all matters related to anti-opium and anti-drug efforts and submit them in writing for discussion at meetings. The Office shall hold two regular meetings each year, but special meetings may be convened in the event of important matters. In order to enhance the efficiency of anti-opium and anti-drug efforts in the various provinces and cities, personnel may be dispatched at any time with the approval of the concurrent Director-General to supervise and evaluate the efforts. Personnel dispatched to the various provinces and cities to supervise anti-opium and anti-drug efforts may handle matters by order of the provincial or municipal government in conjunction with the chairman or mayor of the province or city and may co-sign the statutes. The Office shall have a secretariat and a first and second division.

The General Rules for the Organization of Anti-Opium Committees of the various provinces, cities, and counties consist of sixteen articles. The main points are as follows: The anti-opium committees of the various provinces and cities shall have seven to nine members, and the anti-opium committees of the counties shall have five to seven members, who shall be employed by the provincial, municipal, and county governments from among impartial individuals with a passion for the cause of anti-opium in the local area, and three shall be designated as standing committee members or one shall be designated as the chairman. The Anti-Opium Director-General's Office may dispatch personnel to participate in the anti-opium committees of the various provinces and cities, and the provincial committees may dispatch personnel to participate in the county committees to supervise and handle anti-opium affairs at any time. The anti-opium committees of the various provinces, cities, and counties shall be responsible for supervising, urging, reporting, correcting, and investigating the handling of anti-opium and anti-drug matters by the local governments, but may execute entrusted matters under the orders of the Anti-Opium Director-General's Office. The provincial and municipal anti-opium committees shall establish two sections, and the county committees shall establish two units. The functions of the anti-opium committees of the various provinces, cities, and counties are as follows: 1. Supervising and evaluating anti-opium and anti-drug efforts. 2. Assisting in the investigation of smuggling and examining cases involving opium and drug offenders. 3. Managing opium and drug cessation institutions and planning and allocating their expenses. 4. Reviewing and deliberating on rewards and punishments for anti-opium and anti-drug personnel. 5. Auditing all income and expenditures related to the confiscation of the property of opium and drug offenders. 6. Promoting prohibitions and designing and reviewing drafts of propaganda documents and illustrations. 7. Drafting and editing anti-opium and anti-drug documents and reports on proposals. 8. The anti-opium committees of the various provinces, cities, and counties shall hold one meeting each week, and special meetings may be convened in the event of urgent matters. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

Anti-Opium Director-General's Office Holds 6/3 Commemoration 17

(Nanjing) The Anti-Opium Director-General's Office held a 6/3 Commemoration Meeting at the Lihsheshe at 9:30 AM on the 3rd. The event was attended by over 400 people, including anti-opium committee members Gan Naiguang, Lü Xinchou, Zhang Boling, Zhang Yuanshan, Li Zhonggong, Li Jihong, and representatives from various agencies, including Lü Chao, Liu Ruiheng, Chen Shuru, Jiao Yitang, and Wang Yongbin. After the ceremony, Gan Naiguang, representing Director-General Jiang, presided over the meeting and delivered a speech, and read Director-General Jiang's instructions. Subsequently, Li Shengong reported on the anti-opium situation, followed by a speech by Lü Chao, who stated that our country had suffered from imperialist oppression in the past, and that the scourge continues unabated today, which is truly heartbreaking. Now, Director-General Jiang, based on Premier Sun’s anti-drug instructions and the Central Committee's resolution, is determined to strictly prohibit opium and drugs. If this is achieved, the opium disaster of more than 200 years can be eradicated. Only with a strong body can the whole nation have the ability to resist, and the nation can be revived. Finally, Zhang Boling gave a speech, detailing the determination of our country's anti-drug movement in the past and the reasons for its subsequent failure. In the face of the laxity of the anti-opium administration, Director-General Jiang resolutely shouldered the responsibility of eradicating opium and drugs. The results of the past seven months have been astonishing. Mr. Jiang is using this educational approach to transform the country and revive the nation, and the country's future is expected to be bright. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

Original Text of Director-General Jiang's Instructions 18

Today, we commemorate the day 97 years ago when our anti-opium sage, Lin Wenzhong, burned opium at Humen. When we recall Lin Gong's fearless spirit and unyielding perseverance on that day, we truly feel infinite admiration, and at the same time, we cannot help but feel infinite shame. Our sages, in order to protect the health and survival of the nation, did not hesitate to make any sacrifices to resist the import of foreign opium. Unexpectedly, in the decades since then, the spread of the opium scourge has become increasingly serious. We descendants have truly let down our sages too much. Opium is enough to harm individual health, affect social livelihood, shake the foundation of the country, and hinder the culture of the nation. The severity of the disaster is chilling. Lin Gong's instructions say, "The poison of opium is even worse than floods and wild beasts. There is no one in the world who does not think that opium must be prohibited. If this disaster is not eradicated, there will be no usable soldiers and no funds to be raised in ten years." These are truly accurate words. In history, we can see many precedents. The demise of a nation is often not simply caused by the conquest of another nation with military or political power, but by the degeneration and corruption of the nation itself. Conversely, any foreign aggression and oppression, for a nation with latent power that can strive to become strong, can only be regarded as a temporary blow. No matter how devastated it is, this nation will eventually be able to recover. Therefore, I feel that the danger of opium far outweighs foreign aggression. Whether our nation can be revived depends on whether we can make a great determination, invigorate our spirit, improve our internal affairs, and strengthen our national power. The most important thing is whether we can eradicate the scourge of opium and drugs. In recent years, while suppressing bandits, Zhongzheng has witnessed the widespread and profound suffering of our nation from the scourge of opium and drugs. If this continues, it will not only lead to national ruin but also to the extinction of the race. Therefore, I have made the greatest determination to eliminate this cruel and poisonous harm and have established a plan for a two-year ban on drugs and a six-year ban on opium, and have formulated various regulations to be implemented separately. Since the Central Government has specially granted me authority and responsibility, I have been working diligently every day, deeply fearing that I will not be able to implement it effectively and live up to the expectations of the Central Government and the people. Now, the anti-opium branches in the various provinces and cities have been established one after another, and more than 1.56 million opium addicts have been registered. Examining the actual results, we cannot say that there has been no progress, but in the end, it has not achieved the expected results according to the original plan. The crux of the problem, as I see it, is generally no more than the following: First, there is a lack of firm confidence. Because the prohibition of opium has never been thoroughly achieved throughout history, especially during the warlord era, the so-called prohibition of opium was nothing more than a policy of exploiting the people, and those who handled anti-opium affairs were all engaged in private gain and corruption, causing the general public to be unable to restore their confidence in the government's anti-opium policy for a time. They always thought that the government was simply "collecting taxes under the guise of prohibition" to collect money. Even the civil affairs officials at all levels also harbor the idea of ​​wait-and-see, thinking that it is impossible to eliminate opium and failing to earnestly implement the laws and regulations promulgated by the government. This is really an absolutely unacceptable wrong mentality. If this wrong mentality cannot be broken, the prohibition of opium will never succeed. I have repeatedly stated that the government will never compromise or surrender to the evil forces of opium and that the policy of banning it within a limited time will not be changed in the slightest. The government absolutely has no intention of "collecting taxes under the guise of prohibition" to extend the period of taxation to seek any financial benefits. In the past year or so, the majority of the people have indeed recognized the government's determination to implement the policy. If there are still a few people who are waiting and watching, then it is tantamount to willingly ruining themselves. They should wake up as soon as possible so as not to regret it too late. Second, there is a lack of a practical and hard-working spirit. In the past, the agencies that were in charge of anti-opium efforts were mostly nominal or started out strictly and then became lax, so there were no achievements to speak of. When Chinese people do things and cannot get through, they always like to blame it on the difficult environment. In fact, this is precisely to prove that they themselves do not have the power to transform the environment and overcome difficulties, but are succumbed to the environment. For example, when people with power and influence violate the prohibition orders, anti-opium administrative personnel are often intimidated by their power and influence and are unable to do anything, so they simply muddle along. As a result, they can neither prohibit officials nor prohibit the people, so they have to withdraw and become prisoners of opium. If our future prohibition of opium is still the same as before, with the constant excuse of a difficult environment and the inability to be determined to fight to the end without surrendering, then there is no way to do anything. I believe that there are absolutely no difficulties that cannot be solved in the world, nor are there absolutely no obstacles that cannot be overcome. One point of effort will lead to one point of success. The so-called "sincerity can move mountains," we should take this sentence as our belief. Third, there is a lack of a spirit of cooperation. We know that any social problem is not isolated or one-sided, but is related to the entire society. The opium problem is certainly no exception. If we examine the reasons why ordinary people smoke opium, they are generally no more than the following: 1. The poor social health environment. 2. Using opium as a medicine. 3. Work conditions are too harsh. 4. Curiosity or being seduced by others. In detail analysis, it is related to all aspects of society. Therefore, the prohibition of opium is definitely not a successful effort by partial or one-sided efforts. The entire society must be mobilized, cooperate with each other, and work together firmly towards a common goal in order to achieve results. Moreover, if all sectors of our society, including education, politics, health, and charity, work together unanimously, we can not only ban it within a limited time, but we will certainly be able to ban it ahead of schedule. I believe that only the total power of society is the key to determining everything's success or failure. In short, the most important meaning of commemorating our anti-opium sages here today is to examine our past mistakes, to emulate Lin Gong's spirit of practical and hard work and unyielding efforts, and to hope that the people of the whole country will work together to fight this evil force to the death and achieve the goal. Finally, I cannot but solemnly mention that the future of opium prohibition in China also depends on international cooperation. Because the organizations that illegally sell opium and drugs can exist behind China's territory, which the Chinese government cannot do anything about. This difficult situation is not shared by other countries. If foreign opium and drugs continue to be imported into China, all our efforts and sacrifices will be in vain. I sincerely hope that the friendly countries will not adopt the 90-year-old poisonous policy that the British government has already abandoned towards China, so as to cause this unfortunate phenomenon and increase the reasons for misunderstanding between each other. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Court commemorated 6/3 and burned drugs at 2:00 PM. 70 people from all walks of life attended the viewing. Court President Zhou Zuchen spoke about the significance of the commemoration. A total of 4,828 taels of opium, 5 taels and 7 qian and 9 fen of white powder, 1,220 golden pills, two large bags of heroin, and 33,566 taels of opium, 101 taels and 9 qian of opium paste, 48 taels of opium residue, 187 taels of heroin from the High Court First Branch, and 9 taels of white powder drugs from the Tanggu Branch Court, and a total of 50,000 taels of lactose were burned. The Municipal Government also burned drugs at the drug rehabilitation center at 2:00 PM. Municipal Government Secretary-General Shi Jisheng spoke to over 100 guests about the dangers of drug use. (Special dispatch, 3rd)

Hankou Public Security Bureau Strictly Prohibits Rumors of People Being Harmed by Poison Needles 21

(Hankou) Recently, rumors of people being harmed by poison needles have spread too quickly in Hankou, affecting social order significantly. The reporter asked Chen Xizeng, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, about this matter. According to him, the Hankou Second Branch Bureau recently had a case in which a habitual thief attempted to seize the belongings of a child, Hong Xueqin. Hong Xueqin was young and, upon hearing what his relative had said about the recent rumors of people being stabbed by poison needles, suddenly felt numb due to psychological stimulation. After investigation by the Second Branch Bureau, the original cause was determined to be completely untrue. On the 3rd, the Seventh Branch Bureau also had a similar misunderstanding. After repeated consideration by the bureau and based on his own practical investigation, it was learned that the origin of these rumors was that someone had widely posted advertisements on the walls of various streets, with words stating secret recipes for preventing poison needles. The ignorant men and women in society did not understand and thought that it was true. Currently, in addition to dispelling the rumors, the bureau will issue a notice on the 4th, strictly prohibiting these rumors. If anyone is found to be creating rumors under this pretext, they will be reported to the superiors for strict punishment by military law. (Central News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

Li Zilos Arrives in Kobe, Harboring Plans to Visit Japanese Authorities 23

Increased Purchasing Power of the Chinese People Benefits Britain, America, and Japan

Kobe – Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, economic advisor to the British government, accompanied by his wife and secretary, arrived in Kobe port aboard a Canadian vessel at 4 PM on the 2nd, for another visit to Japan. He told reporters on the ship that the purpose of this visit was to further discuss matters from last year's trip to China, where he had extensive talks with Japanese authorities, but some issues remained unresolved. He plans to meet with Foreign Minister Arita and two or three other key figures in Tokyo. However, he emphasized that his trip to China was not as a political advisor but as an economic advisor, allowing him to adjust the interests between Japan and China, and Japan and Britain from a third-party perspective. Regarding the economic and financial reconstruction of China, he believes it can be achieved with Japan's cooperation. He noted that the recent currency reform in China did not link the Chinese currency to the British pound or US dollar, so as long as the Chinese currency is stable, it will not be affected by fluctuations in the British pound or US dollar. If China's currency reform can stabilize the Chinese currency, it will benefit Britain, America, and Japan. In short, providing the Chinese people with sufficient purchasing power will undoubtedly create a vast new market. He has several trial proposals for this, but because they are trial proposals, he cannot disclose them. (3rd, Domei News Agency)

Japanese Investigation Team Departs to Develop Cotton in North China 24

(Tokyo) Taking advantage of the US and Australia raising tariffs, Japanese government and private sectors strongly advocate establishing a raw material policy for cotton, wool, and other materials. They plan to steadily implement production increase plans for cotton in Korea, Taiwan, and Manchuria. On the other hand, regarding the pending development of cotton in North China, although they have adopted a passive attitude due to concerns about maintaining security, the urgency of cotton self-sufficiency has led them to decide to take the first step in developing cotton in North China. They have decided to form a North China Cotton Investigation Team composed of private sector operators and government representatives. The names of the members are as follows:

Government: Takahashi, official from the Colonial Industry Bureau of the Ministry of Colonial Affairs.

Private Sector: Danjo Kenichi (Nagasaki Spinning), representative of the Spinning Federation; Ikeda Zenkichi (Toyo Cotton), representative of the Cotton Traders Association; Hiraoka Kotaro (Director of the same association), representative of the Spinning Federation in China.

Takahashi, representing the government, departed on the night of the 1st. The private sector representatives are also scheduled to depart within days for a period of approximately 40 days. They will focus on Hebei, Shandong, Suiyuan, and Chahar, investigating cultivation results and consulting with local military and Chinese dignitaries. In addition, a wool investigation team for North China will soon be organized as a separate group, with several individuals, including Hashi Jinbei, representing the Japan Wool Industry Association, and private operators participating. (3rd, Domei News Agency)

Japanese Privy Council Passes Japan-Manchukuo Treaty 25

(Tokyo) A plenary session of the Privy Council was held at the Imperial Palace at 10 AM on the morning of the 3rd to deliberate on the Japan-Manchukuo treaty. Chairman Hiranuma, Vice-Chairman Arai, councilors, Secretary-General Murakami, government officials, Prime Minister Hirota, Foreign Minister Arita, Minister of the Army Sugiyama, Minister of Justice Hayashi, Director-General of the Legislation Bureau Kida, Director of the Treaty Bureau Kuriyama, and others attended. Under the Emperor's presence, they deliberated on the "Abolition of a portion of extraterritorial rights in Manchukuo and other treaties and annexes between Japan and Manchukuo." First, Chairman Arai reported on the committee's deliberation process and results on the case. Then, the original proposal from the committee chairman's report was unanimously approved. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 AM. (3rd, Domei News Agency)

Fuzhou Cracks Down on Counterfeit Coin Manufacturing Organization 32

Established by Taiwanese Sun Guangming; Tens of Thousands of Yuan in Counterfeit Money Seized

(Xiamen) Counterfeit subsidiary currency notes from the Fujian Provincial Bank are rampant, making it difficult to distinguish between genuine and fake notes, and merchants are almost refusing to use them. On the 3rd, the Public Security Bureau, in conjunction with Japanese police, raided a large-scale counterfeit money manufacturing organization in the upstairs of the Xingfa Foreign Firm opened by Taiwanese Sun Guangming on Datong Road. Sun fled, but tens of thousands of yuan in counterfeit 10-cent, 20-cent, and 50-cent Fujian Provincial Bank notes were seized, along with more than ten glass plates for the aforementioned counterfeit notes, as well as chemical solutions, inks, printing presses, etc. Glass plates for counterfeit 10-yuan Kwangtung Provincial Bank notes and 5-yuan notes were also seized. Wu Qiuxiang and Li Shanmin were arrested. During the police raid, someone fired more than a dozen shots at the police from a nearby alleyway, but no one was injured. The police pursued the suspect, who fled into a certain foreign firm on Jukou Street. The detective team learned that Sun Guangming had been engaged in the business of manufacturing counterfeit money for some time and had been manufacturing and selling counterfeit money in Shanghai three or four years ago before bringing it to Fujian. (3rd, Special Dispatch)

Organizational Regulations of the Personnel Assessment Office 47

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council approved that personnel assessment agencies should still be established at the provincial level, but they should be renamed Provincial Personnel Assessment Offices. After being sent to the Legislative Yuan for further discussion, the Yuan approved and sent it to the Legislative Committee for review, which has been completed. The title of the case has been set as the "Organizational Regulations of the Personnel Assessment Office," with a full text of nine articles. It stipulates that the Ministry of Personnel Assessment may establish Personnel Assessment Offices in various provinces to handle the personnel assessment of commissioned civil servants in the respective provinces or neighboring provinces and cities. Each office will have one director and two sections: General Affairs and Review. The case will be submitted to the Yuan's meeting for review on the 5th. (3rd, Central News Agency)

Continuation of Civil Servants' Aviation Contribution from July 48

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan passed the "Measures for Continuing the Collection of Civil Servants' Aviation Contribution" at its meeting on the 2nd. The main points are as follows: All personnel of party, government, military, and police agencies nationwide, as well as faculty and staff of public schools, should donate a certain percentage of their actual salary to the government for the construction of aviation. The donation period is from July and will last for one year. The monthly donation standards are: No donation for salaries below 50 yuan; 1% for 51-100 yuan; 1.5% for 101-150 yuan; 2% for 151-200 yuan; 2.5% for 201-300 yuan; 3% for 301-400 yuan; 3.5% for 401-600 yuan; and 4% for those above 600 yuan. The donations should be collected and remitted monthly to the Aviation Construction Association or the Central Bank in Shanghai. (3rd, Central News Agency)

Ministry of Railways Stipulates Measures for Land Acquisition for Road Construction 49

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways stipulated the "Provisional Measures for Land Acquisition for Railway Construction," which were submitted to and passed by the Executive Yuan. The full text of 17 articles stipulates that after surveying and determining the price of land for railway construction, the railway engineering agency should draw a map of the boundaries according to the scope of the determined route and submit it to fulfill the legal procedures. According to Article 365 of the Land Law, they can immediately enter the boundary to start construction. Land acquisition should be sufficient for railway use and various construction lands necessary in the future. (3rd, Special Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegrams

June 3rd Reuters Exclusive Commercial Telegram 62

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Somewhat looser today, falling four pence from yesterday to 138 shillings and 10 pence.

London Big Spreads: Quiet today, spot and futures both at 19 pence and 9375, each up 0.0625. China and speculators sold, India bought, but not much was sold.

Montevideo Big Spreads: Futures opened strong this morning, July contracts rose 18 pounds sterling to 45.00-45.30.

Exchange Rates

British-American: London foreign exchange market firm this morning, with the British-American exchange rate opening at $5.00125, up 15625 from yesterday's closing rate. It continued to rise 875 at 11 AM, another 625 at 12:30 PM, and again 125 at 1 PM, to $5.0175.

Securities

New York: Mixed securities market this morning, with prices showing a downward trend. Merchants are feeling uneasy about this situation. At the same time, the political and financial situation in France is also putting general pressure on the market. Speculators are buying and selling, and prices are not fluctuating much. At noon, the prices of major securities were down by half a pound sterling from yesterday's closing price, while some were up by 125. Demand for steel stocks is very good, and the market remained stable before noon. The prices of New York securities are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: Stable today, with favorable weather news for the long side causing a lot of speculative buying. Trading was light before noon. At noon, the October contract was at 10.88, up eight pounds sterling from yesterday's closing price.

Liverpool Cotton Market: Futures stable today, with the July contract up four pounds sterling at 1 PM to 6.22.

Liverpool: Wheat opened firm due to higher overseas telegrams and news of poor harvests in the Canadian spring wheat region, but the market then calmed down slightly due to news of slightly cold weather in the United States. Chicago Wheat: Futures stable this morning, with continuous dry conditions in the Northwest region inducing some speculative buying. At noon, the September contract was at 84625, up 125 from yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

Argentina Formally Requests Early Convening of the League of Nations Assembly to Handle the Italo-Abyssinian Crisis and Reform Issues; Roughly Expected to be Convened on the 23rd of this Month 65

(Geneva) Argentina is strongly opposed to Italy's annexation of Abyssinia and recently made a verbal request for the League of Nations Assembly to convene an emergency meeting to consider sanctions against Italy. Today, it sent a diplomatic note to the League of Nations Secretariat, reiterating this proposal. In addition to sanctions, Argentina also requests consideration of: 1. The situation arising from the annexation of Abyssinia. 2. Reform of the League of Nations. Argentina suggests that the League of Nations Assembly should be convened around June 16th, and the member states of the League of Nations should deal with the new situation created by the annexation. After receiving this diplomatic note, the League of Nations Secretariat immediately notified the Chairman of the Assembly, Dr. Benes, who must consult with the Chairman of the League of Nations Executive Council, British Foreign Secretary Eden, and others before a date can be selected for the Assembly to convene. It is reported that other Latin American countries have agreed to support Argentina's proposal not to recognize Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. (3rd, Reuters)

(Geneva) Argentine representative to the League of Nations, Mr. Genochio, visited League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol at half past six in the afternoon, where he formally presented a note requesting the early convening of the Assembly. The contents of the note had been previously notified to representatives of South American countries. The note stated that the Executive Council had previously decided on the 12th of last month to postpone the discussion of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute until the 16th of this month. At that time, the Argentine representative had already submitted a reservation. It was also stated that the League of Nations is based on the principle of equality. Therefore, important issues such as the Italo-Abyssinian dispute should be discussed jointly by all member states. "The government of our country now believes that the League of Nations should discuss the situation caused by Italy's annexation of Abyssinia and the implementation of sanctions and therefore applies to call the assembly early." Avenol, after receiving the note, is scheduled to discuss the matter with the current chairman of the Assembly, Czech President Benes, and the current chairman of the Executive Council, British Foreign Secretary Eden, tomorrow. He will also make informal contacts with other governments in order to decide whether the Assembly should be convened earlier. According to League of Nations personnel, Argentina's request should be accepted by the League of Nations. According to this agency's diplomatic correspondent, the Assembly will most likely be convened early on the 23rd of this month, and the extraordinary meeting of the Executive Council will also be postponed to that day. League of Nations personnel commented on the note submitted by Argentina, saying that it is based on the spirit of democracy of the League of Nations and has sufficient reason. Because the League of Nations Assembly includes all member states, large and small, on an equal footing, its method is the most democratic in all the activities of the League of Nations. Argentina also repeatedly cited Article 10 of the Covenant in the note and the principle of not recognizing land seized by force. The former stipulates that the territorial integrity of the member states of the League of Nations should be respected and maintained, and the latter is a principle consistently supported by the countries of South America. In addition, it is also worth noting that the word "annexation" is deliberately used in the note. In Italy's formal declarations, it has always tried to avoid using this term. (2nd, Havas)

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden received Argentine Ambassador Mabrun today in the afternoon to discuss the country's request to call the League of Nations assembly earlier. However, the talks were purely informal in nature, so Foreign Secretary Eden did not formally express the British government's views to the Argentine Ambassador. Political figures said that the British government did not advocate an earlier convening of the League of Nations Assembly, but if Argentina's request is supported by other countries, Britain would have no objections. (2nd, Havas)

The Emperor of Abyssinia Arrives in London 66

(Sandown) The Emperor of Abyssinia, accompanied by members of the royal family, arrived at this port at 1:00 PM today aboard the British mail ship "Oxford," and immediately traveled to London by train. (Havas News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

(London) The Emperor of Abyssinia, aboard the British mail ship "Oxford," received an interview from a reporter from the Daily Telegraph. The reporter asked if he was preparing to go to Geneva to personally attend the League of Nations meeting to defend Abyssinia's position. The Emperor replied, "Everything must wait until after arriving in England to be decided. We are eager to contact the authorities of various European countries to understand their attitudes towards our position. The people of the Ethiopian Empire have repeatedly expressed their trust in the League of Nations and their emphasis on the moral value of the Covenant. We will certainly adhere to the resolutions passed by the League of Nations, striving for their continued implementation, and the Covenant of the League of Nations must be respected. We deeply believe that the Italo-Ethiopian dispute should be resolved based on justice. Although Italy has occupied Abyssinia by force, it has been judged by the League of Nations as an aggressor, and its actions cannot be recognized. Abyssinia still exists in law, and the southwestern part of Abyssinia still has a government in practice, which continues to handle state affairs under my command before I leave the country. In terms of war, if the enemy troops had followed the laws of war, the outcome would not be certain to this day, because our army fought bravely and repeatedly defeated strong enemies, until the Italian army used poison gas, our army began to falter, therefore we will never admit defeat." (Havas News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

(London) The Emperor of Abyssinia departed from the Port of Gibraltar for England. It is estimated that he will arrive here in the afternoon of tomorrow. The Emperor's visit is of a private nature, so the authorities do not intend to officially send guards to protect him, but the Emperor will spend funds to hire several police officers to provide constant protection. A joint conference of British organizations supporting the League of Nations will hold a large-scale meeting in "Albert Hall" here in the coming days to discuss the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. It is rumored that the Emperor will be invited to attend and deliver a speech, but confirmation is awaited. (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

French Labor Strikes Expand 74

Strikers in More Than Two Hundred Factories

(Paris) The number of factories affected by the labor strikes in the capital area has reached more than two hundred and thirty, including metallurgical plants, aircraft manufacturing plants, chemical food plants, and gas plants. The number of striking workers occupying factory buildings has reached more than 100,000. In addition, one hundred and twenty-eight workers at famous swimming pools and dance halls also went on strike to protest increased taxes. Moreover, labor strikes in the provinces are now more serious, with more than 10,000 striking workers, especially in the northern industrial area. For example, 1,150 workers at the Peugeot car factory and 1,000 workers at the Achiet electrical plant went on strike this morning and occupied the factory buildings. (Havas dispatch, 3rd)

(Paris) The movement of striking by staying in the factory but not working is now spreading like wildfire. After the strikers in the machine industry achieved their demands, other industries followed suit one after another, and the speed was amazing. It is reported that there are more than 70 strikers in the bus company. At the same time, many large factories such as Citroen and the Nieport aircraft factory have returned to work as usual. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(Paris) The metallurgical industry strike, which had shown signs of ending quickly yesterday, suddenly took a turn for the worse today. The factory buildings of seventy factories are still occupied by strikers who refuse to leave. In addition, the strike situation in various chemical factories and food factories has also worsened. Previously, the strike was only limited to the capital area, but now it has spread to other areas in the suburbs. Even workers in the provinces have started to follow suit, especially in the northern industrial cities, such as Lille and Valenciennes. Although some factories in the metallurgical industry in the capital area have returned to work as usual, all the workers are still restless. For example, workers at the Renault car factory held many demonstrations, and workers at the Caudron aircraft factory stopped working again shortly after resuming work. Capitalists now believe that the strike no longer has an occupational nature, but has a political meaning. This can be seen from the fact that some of the strike leaders are not employees of the factory. Therefore, the joint meeting of labor and capital in the metallurgical industry is experiencing difficulties, and it is doubtful whether the union representatives can sign the work contract with the workers as scheduled (previously said it could be signed tomorrow). Some strikers have arbitrarily detained the managers of the factories. Premier Sarraut has received reports of this situation and immediately summoned union representatives to order them to take necessary measures immediately to stop it. The representatives have agreed to do so. (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

(Paris) The striking workers in the metallurgical industry in the capital area are still occupying the factory buildings and refusing to leave. The unions recently issued a statement explaining the reasons, stating that there are a total of 250,000 workers in the metallurgical industry. The capitalists have only accepted the demands put forward by 100,000 workers, and the remaining 150,000 are still disappointed. Once these people are satisfied, the strike will naturally end. As for the workers in other industries, they have joined the strike because their wages are too low. (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

New French Cabinet Personnel 75

There will be Two Women

(Paris) Socialist leader Blum is now organizing a new government according to completely new principles. The main personnel who have been internally determined are: Foreign Minister Delbos, Army Minister Lyautey, Defense Minister Daladier, and Finance Minister Auriol. There will be two women in the new government, which is an innovation: one is Mrs. Lacore, who will serve as Deputy State Member for Children's Welfare, and the other is Mrs. Joliot-Curie, the daughter of the famous scientist Marie Curie, who discovered radium, who will serve as Deputy State Member for Scientific Exploration. (Reuters dispatch, 3rd)

(Paris) Regarding the candidates for the new cabinet members, the gist has been recorded in yesterday's telegram. The news that was revealed in the lounge of the Chamber of Deputies this afternoon is exactly the same as what our reporter has learned. There is no change in the candidates for all important cabinet members. The only differences are the following: Yesterday's telegram said that the three departments of the Navy, Army, and Air Force will be merged into the Ministry of National Defense, with three chiefs in charge of naval, army, and air force affairs, respectively. Now it is learned that the six departments of the Navy, Army, Aviation, Agriculture, Posts and Telecommunications, and Merchant Marine have all been changed to directorates, each with a director, but no chief. The position of Director of the Navy Directorate, which yesterday's telegram intended to be filled by Congressman Campinchi, is now known to be filled by Congressman Holion, a radical socialist. The position of Chief of Overseas Affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which yesterday's telegram intended to be selected from Congressman Tedsang of the Radical Socialist Party and Congressman Moch of the Socialist Party, is now known to be filled by Congressman Modet of the Socialist Party. Yesterday's telegram said that Mrs. Lecare will be the Chief of the Ministry of Agriculture. It is now known that she will be changed to the Director of the Ministry of Public Health. Originally, Mr. Umbrum intended to appoint Mrs. Joliot-Curie (the daughter of Marie Curie, the inventor of radium) as the Director of the Ministry of Public Health, but she firmly declined the position, so Mrs. Lecare was appointed instead. The candidates for the ministers of the newly established Ministry of National Solidarity and the Ministry of National Economy are unknown. In addition, the Daily News recently criticized the structure of the new cabinet, roughly saying, "The future Prime Minister Leon Blum intends to add more director positions, which is tantamount to restoring the councilors of the monarchical era in the past. In the future, the ministers will have the support of the directors, and their administration can achieve great efficiency, and a new factor can also be added to the administrative organization. Moreover, the ministers of each department are all rich in experience and superior in learning, which will naturally benefit the cabinet and will not be restricted by trivial department affairs, but will be able to engage in greater and farther-reaching matters. However, Leon Blum and his associates are still strictly silent about the new cabinet organization. The above is just speculation." (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

Japanese Dr. Yaoi Invents New Vaccination Method 78

Vaccine Injected Subcutaneously

(Tokyo) Since Edward Jenner's vaccination with cowpox, which has made great contributions to mankind, the year 1936 marks the 140th anniversary. At that time, all smallpox vaccinations were done by inoculation, so the ugly smallpox scars were a common worry for women around the world. In Showa year 5, Dr. Hideo Yaoi, a member of the Japanese Institute of Infectious Diseases, discovered and successfully created a method of subcutaneous vaccination with refined vaccine (vaccination by injection). In the past six years, after a period of careful testing, the result was that President Nagayo of Tokyo Imperial University petitioned for permission to publicly sell this unique refined vaccine using the new vaccination method. Now, with the approval of the two ministers of the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior, it will be announced in the official gazette by the Ministry of Education on the same day, and will be sold publicly by the Institute of Infectious Diseases. Japan, ahead of other advanced countries in the world, is implementing this new vaccination method, which is a major reform in the world of vaccination since Jenner. At the same time, it will also promote a major revision of the Japanese Vaccination Law Regulations, which stipulates a dedicated vaccination method. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 3rd)

Panchen Lama to Arrive in Labrang in Ten Days 79

Japanese in Qingdao Stir Up Trouble: International Negotiations Sparked by Assault on Japanese Elementary School Student 80

Qingdao Correspondence: Since Japan increased its troops stationed in North China, the situation there has become exceptionally tense. Japanese vagrants residing in Qingdao constantly seek opportunities to cause trouble and disrupt the overall situation. However, due to the city authorities' thorough precautions, they have found no excuse to do so, and peace has been maintained. Recently, a Japanese elementary school student was reportedly assaulted by an unknown person. The Japanese saw this as an opportunity and made a mountain out of a molehill, creating an intimidating atmosphere and protesting vehemently to the municipal government, which has led to significant negotiations. The details of the incident and the negotiations are described below.

Incident Account: On the 29th of last month, around 5 p.m., a nine-year-old female student from the First Japanese Elementary School on Bao'an Road was playing at the Japanese sports ground on Rehe Road. At that time, a child (nationality unclear) injured the girl's right arm. The child fled after the incident. Around 6 p.m., two students from the Municipal Elementary School on Huangtai Road, Jiang Wanshan (14 years old) and Yu Cifu (12 years old), who were in the second-highest grade, were returning home after school was dismissed. They passed by the Japanese sports ground and were seized by the girl's parents, who insisted that they were the ones who had injured the girl. They beat and kicked Jiang and Yu, and then sent Jiang Wanshan to the Japanese police station for detention. Yu Cifu was released at the time because of his young age. This is the general account of the incident.

Details of Negotiations: After this incident, the Japanese believed that Chinese elementary school students dared to assault Japanese elementary school students because they were taught anti-Japanese education in school. The Japanese Residents' Association, Youth League, and other groups held an emergency meeting the day after the incident to discuss how to respond. They also requested the Japanese consul to lodge a protest with the municipal government. Upon receiving the news, the municipal government immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to retrieve Jiang Wanshan from the Japanese police station for interrogation. According to Jiang's statement, the school had designated this week as a "Cleanliness Campaign Week," so every day after school was dismissed at 5 p.m., they had to carry out a major cleaning work for one hour until around 6 p.m. On the evening of the 29th, after work, he waited for the cleaning work to be completed as usual, and at 6:20 p.m., he went home with his classmate Yu Cifu. Unexpectedly, when they arrived at the Japanese sports ground, they were seized and beaten by the Japanese. He claimed not to know who injured the Japanese girl. The Public Security Bureau summoned several of Jiang's classmates to the bureau for questioning. Jiang's classmates all stated that Jiang did not leave the school until after 6 p.m. on that day and had not taken a step out of the school gate before 6 p.m. However, the Japanese insisted that Jiang was the culprit and must be severely punished. The Japanese Youth League sent representatives to the municipal government every day to make a fuss, slapping the table and using disrespectful language. The Japanese consulate also put forward unreasonable demands to the municipal government: 1. The mayor should personally apologize to the Japanese consul. 2. Replace the Director of the Education Bureau, Dang Fazhang. 3. Revise the elementary school textbooks to remove anti-Japanese sentiments. 4. Guarantee that the same incident will not occur again. The Japanese Youth League even threatened that if their demands were not met, they would telegraph Japan and request the naval department to send warships to Qingdao for protection. The municipal government was deeply concerned that the incident would escalate and become difficult to handle. In addition to the repeated attempts at mediation by the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Hu Jiafeng, and his earnest negotiations with the Japanese consul, the mayor, Shen Honglie, was away on official business in Beijing and Shanghai. He was urgently telegraphed to return to Qingdao to handle everything. After receiving the telegram, Shen returned to Qingdao by China Aviation flight at 1:30 a.m. today (the 2nd) from Shanghai. According to Secretary-General Hu, the unreasonable demands put forward by the Japanese to the municipal government due to the assault on the elementary school student have been sternly rejected by the municipal government. After the mayor returns to Qingdao, he will formally negotiate with the Japanese side to resolve this matter as soon as possible to avoid further complications.

Huainan Railway: Opening Ceremony on June 5th (Continued) Simultaneously Celebrating the Sixth Anniversary of the Coal Mine Completion of the Railway 81

Original Purpose of Building the Road:

The Huainan mining area is located between Huaiyuan and Shou counties in Anhui Province, more than ten miles north of the Hun River. For the transport of coal, although a light railway has been built to reach the Luozhen town on the shore of the Huai River, the coal must still be transported via the Huai River waterway, then transferred to the Jinpu Railway at Pukou, and then sold to various ports. This process of boat and train transfer is difficult to schedule, and the transportation costs are high. The cost of transportation is huge, so the cost is high. Therefore, in order to develop the business of the Bureau and increase the position of domestic coal in the coal market, it is necessary to find a shortcut for transportation. This is the original intention of the Bureau to build the Huainan Railway. Northern Anhui has long been a prosperous area. The Huai River runs across it, and the Feishui flows vertically, gathering lakes and pools between the Yangtze and Huai Rivers. Therefore, agricultural products are especially abundant. After meeting their own needs, they can still be transported to other places for sale. However, in recent years, natural disasters have occurred frequently, and banditry has risen from time to time. Refugees are everywhere, and cultivated land is barren. Farmers are forced by the environment, and they plan to sell their products as soon as they are harvested. In addition, the market scope is narrow, and transportation is extremely difficult, so prices are even lower. The rich cannot live in peace and move to other places. The poor cannot enjoy their work and become even more impoverished. The vitality has been damaged, and few rural villages have not gone bankrupt. Therefore, the construction of the railway, although for the convenience of transporting coal, is also charged with the great mission of reviving the rural areas of northern Anhui.

Extremely Rapid Construction

From the survey and determination of the line to the complete opening of the line, the road took two years. The entire line runs from Tianjia'an on the Huai River in the north to Yuxikou on the Yangtze River in the south, with a main line of 215 kilometers, a branch line of 10 kilometers, and a siding line of about 35 kilometers. The total cost of general affairs, survey, track sleepers, bridges and culverts, stones, track sleepers, stations and houses, and machinery is about 4.8 million yuan in national currency. Calculated on the basis of 215 kilometers of main line, the construction cost per kilometer is about 22,300 yuan. If the 225 kilometers of main line and branch line are combined, the construction cost per kilometer is only 21,300 yuan. Adding in the locomotives and vehicles worth 1.34 million yuan in national currency, the total is about 6.1 million yuan. Calculated on the basis of 215 kilometers, the cost per kilometer is only 28,300 yuan. Moreover, the general affairs expenses of more than 160,000 yuan in the above-mentioned 6.1 million yuan only account for 2.62% of the total cost. Because the engineering equipment has standards and cannot be careless, it is necessary to strive for economy in the general affairs item. Subsequently, with the daily increase in coal production and the abundance of products along the line, passenger and freight transportation is very promising. In order to fully develop the railway's effectiveness, it is necessary to prepare more locomotives and vehicles. Therefore, after the winter of the 23rd year, vehicles worth more than one million yuan were added. However, it is impossible to raise funds by oneself, and the domestic economic situation at this time is extremely serious. The banking industry is quite hesitant about guaranteeing payment, and it has taken a lot of effort to see a start. In addition, the road runs through the Jianghuai area, and Tianjia'an and Yuxikou should have large-scale wharves to connect with shipping. The construction of the wharf at Yuxikou, which is now a hub for coal transportation, is particularly urgent. In the midst of extreme difficulties in raising funds, the business was operated diligently and the construction was carried out with great effort. Now, large vehicles with a load of more than 5,000 tons can be docked, and coal transportation is becoming more and more smooth.

Geography and Products, Population and Resources

Regarding the geography, population, products, and mineral resources along the Huainan Railway, the following is a special description for the purpose of observing the general situation of the areas passed by the railway, and the mission it undertakes. The counties and towns passed by the railway include Tianjia'an, Huainan Mining Area, Shuijiahu, Zhuxiang, Xiatangji, Luoji, Shuangdunji, Hefei, Cuozhen, Qiaotouji, Jiongxiyang River, Zhonghan, Chaoxian, Lintou, Dongguan, Tongchengzha, Shenjiaxiang, and Yuxizhen. Among them, Hefei County is an important area in central Anhui, located in the heart of the Jianghuai area, connecting Lu'an, reaching Anqing in the southwest, Chaowu in the southeast, and Bengbu in the north. Military strategists throughout history have regarded it as a must-contend place. In the past, transportation routes included the Feishui River from the county seat, 70 miles to Shikou, crossing Chaohu Lake southwest to Sanhe, and northeast to Chaowu, all with small steamers operating. From the county seat to Chaoxian, and from Chaoxian to Wuhu, each 180 miles, ordinary upstream and downstream travel takes two days to reach. In spring and winter, the water is shallow and operations must be suspended. The highways include the Chaohe section, the Heye section (currently only通通to Lu'an), the Anhe section, and the Hebei section. However, the roadbeds of each road are not strong, and they must be shut down when it rains or snows. Now that the Huainan Railway has been completed, goods and merchants can take this route north to Luyu, Pingjin, and south to the ports along the Yangtze River. The suffering of stagnation and obstruction will be eliminated from now on. The population of the entire county is about 1.3 million, and the county seat is about 70,000 to 80,000 people. Chaoxian County is the ancient Nan'yi land, where Cheng Tang exiled Jie to Nanchao, which is this place. It borders Chaohu Lake in the west, Hanshan in the east, Hefei in the north, and Wuwei in the south, 180 miles to Wuhu. Small steamers operate, but the journey takes a day. The scenery is quite similar to that of Jiangnan. The products are abundant and sufficient for self-sufficiency. The population of the entire county is about 340,000, and the county seat is close to 70,000 people. The population of other towns ranges from more than 11,000 to more than 1,600. In terms of products, there are coal, wheat, miscellaneous grains, oil, and tobacco in Huaiyuan County; rice, wheat, sorghum, beans, sesame, pigs, oil, chickens, eggs, and tobacco in Shou County; rice, wheat, peanuts, beans, cotton, rapeseed, oil, chickens, eggs, wine, goose and duck feathers in Hefei County; rice, cotton, peanuts, beans, eggs, hairy fish, bricks, tiles, and lime in Chaoxian County; rice, beans, rapeseed, ramie, eggs, ducks, balloonflower in Hanshan County; rice, wheat, beans, cotton, rapeseed, fish, ducks, etc. in Hexian County. The sales locations are the ports along the Yangtze River and the counties in central Anhui.

A Selection of Places of Interest

The Huainan Railway starts from the Huai River in the north and reaches the Yangtze River in the south, running through northern and central Anhui. The cities and towns along the line have been places of must-contend for military strategists throughout history. The southern section is even more frequently seen in historical records. As for the natural scenery, Mount Gui, between Hefei and Chao Lake, is a natural north-south boundary. To the north of the mountain, the plains are vast and boundless, with interconnected fields and scattered villages. The towering blockhouses are often seen, like tigers squatting majestically, all of which are the scenery of North China. To the south of the mountain, the mountains are clear and the waters are beautiful, with lush bamboo and trees, crisscrossing rivers, and sails facing each other, all belonging to the scenery of Jiangnan. The more notable ones are listed below.

Bao Gong Mound: Outside the south gate of Hefei, there is a small mound called Bao Gong Mound, with a temple on it called Bao Gong Temple, with magnificent architecture, dedicated to Song Dynasty's Bao Xiaosu, commonly known as "King Yama Bao." Next to the temple is Bao Gong's reading place, with a stone statue. Below the mound is a small river like a belt, the environment is called Bao River south of the city, flowing east into the Fei River. The river is covered with water chestnuts and lotus roots, and in the height of summer, the red and white lotus flowers decorate the green lotus fields. Small boats are swaying in it, forgetting the summer heat, and feeling carefree. Xiaoyaojin: In the northwest of Hefei city, there are few residents, and Xiaoyaojin is located there. The old trees stand tall, the water is as smooth as a mirror, clear enough to reflect the shadows, about ten miles around, with three or five stone beams to allow passage. Xuanwu Lake in Nanjing is similar to it. Zhang Liao of the Three Kingdoms Wei once defeated Sun Quan's 100,000 troops here with 800 people. There is Zhang Liao's tomb in the northwest, and Li Hongzhang's prime minister's residence about half a mile to the south, still standing majestically. Guishan: Three miles northwest of Chaoxian County, the entire mountain is made of stone, shaped like a turtle, with its head facing Chaohu Lake, as if drinking. Looking around from the mountain, hundreds of miles around can be seen at a glance. The smoke and waves in the lake are vast and full of love, with different scenes in the four seasons and different colors in the morning and evening, truly a beautiful sight. Banyang: Fifteen miles north of Chaoxian County, there is a hot spring called Banyang, naturally forming several pools, the larger ones are square and broad, the smaller ones are seven or eight feet in diameter, clear to the bottom, with bubbles rising like beads, and aquatic plants growing, with small fish swimming in between. More than a dozen residents all take baths here, saying that it has miraculous effects on skin diseases. Chaohu Lake: The source of the lake is in Chaoxian County, which later sank into a lake, with 360 ports and rivers, collecting the waters of Chaoxian, Hefei, Lujiang, and Shucheng, pouring into the Yangtze River, and is a giant swamp in western Huai. In addition to the above-mentioned places, along the line, such as Mingjiao Temple in Hefei, Li's Ancestral Hall in Dayuji, Jile Temple in Chaoxian, Dahu Temple in Changgangji, and Wenbi Pagoda in Dongguan, each has its own strengths, not grand and magnificent.

German Professor at Henan University, Di Lunzi, Assassinated: Body Unharmed, Skull Shattered 82

Kaifeng Correspondence: Di Lunzi, a German professor of German at the Medical College of Henan University, was assassinated last night near the northeast city wall behind the Iron Pagoda in the school. Cao Jinshun, a worker who went to build the forest park this morning, discovered the body and immediately reported it to Yang Songling, a police officer at the Third Precinct in the northern district. After hearing the news, the school also reported it to the provincial government, causing a sensation in the city. People came to view the body in an endless stream. There were no wounds on the body, but the skull was stained with blood, the eyes and nose were unchanged, and all the hair was gone, as if it had been shaved off with a knife. Upon inspecting the back of his straw hat, there was a hole, possibly a gunshot wound. However, his valuable platinum watch, ring, and glasses were all there, indicating that the murder was not committed for robbery. Furthermore, he had only come to Henan University to teach in September last year. Because he could not speak Chinese, he had few social interactions and was dedicated to his duties, and was quite admired by students, so it did not seem to be a case of adultery or revenge. According to Zhang Jingwu, Dean of the Medical College of Henan University, Di lived in Xiyiqi at Henan University and ate his meals at the Huayang Hotel on East Street, boarding there. He was accustomed to taking a walk near the Iron Pagoda every evening after dinner. He taught German for 13 hours a week and did not receive a salary from the school. He was one of four German college professors selected by the German government at the request of the Sino-German Cultural Association to come to China for voluntary teaching to promote Sino-German cultural exchange. He was 34 years old and had no family members in Bian (Kaifeng) (1st).

Wuxi: Appealing for Higher Cocoon Prices 86

The County Farmers' Association of this county stated that the Cocoon Industry Association is currently controlled by the Wuxi Xinxing Silk Factory Trust. At the members' meeting held on May 31, the price of fresh cocoons was deliberately lowered to 30 yuan, ignoring the blood and capital of the silkworm farmers in the four rural areas, causing the farmers to feel a great threat. The association only cared for profits, which is extremely hateful. Although the method proposed by the National Economic Commission Sericulture Improvement Association sets the standard for fresh cocoons at 30 yuan per picul, it should still be adjusted according to the rise and fall of silk prices. The association's method violates the original proposal and is close to deceiving the public. In order to manipulate the market and protect the vital interests of the farmers in the entire county, it specially telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and the Jiangsu Construction Department yesterday, appealing to them to immediately notify the Wuxi County Government to order the Cocoon Industry Association to revise the price of fresh cocoons to 40 yuan per picul based on the actual situation. Although farmers still suffer losses, it is fairer in terms of principle. In addition, Yangming Township in the Third District has convened temporary emergency Baojia meetings with the farmers for several days, and it has been decided that fresh cocoons will not be sold unless the price is 50 or 60 yuan per picul. They would rather discard them and appeal to the County Farmers' Association for relief to alleviate the farmers' suffering.

Yesterday was the June 3rd Anti-Smoking Memorial Day. Next, Cui Dehua, the section chief of the special commissioner's office, County Mayor Long Tiyiao, and Hou Baosan gave speeches successively, all of which won the approval of the audience. Finally, the burning of confiscated smoking paraphernalia began. For a time, the flames were fierce, and the onlookers applauded and cheered. Changzhou: General Meeting of the Cocoon Industry Association 88

The Wuyi Cocoon Industry Association held a general meeting of members on the 2nd. More than 150 members attended the meeting, chaired by Zhao Songping. Matters for discussion: The business tax should be paid in accordance with the Wuxi resolution method, calculated at 80% of 0.5%, which was approved. How should the two-corner business fee of the association be collected? It was resolved that 1.5 cents would be collected for each picul of dried cocoons, borne by the business sector, and a letter would be sent to each cocoon company for verification. The collection procedures would be handled by the Farmers' Bank. Regarding the price of fresh cocoons, it was resolved that the improved variety would be set at 30 yuan per picul, and the local variety would be set at 21 yuan per picul. Zhao Songping, the chairman, proposed to resign, which was approved.

Haizhou: Three Ships Dug Out of the Silted Yellow River 89

There is a silted Yellow River in Guanyun County, which has not been dredged for many years. The county government is now dredging it to straighten out water conservancy and facilitate drainage. The other day, the river dredging mud workers dug up three large ships in the Zhuzha area of the river. One ship was fully loaded with porcelain, one ship was fully loaded with bamboo poles, and one cabin was loaded with dozens of kilograms of platinum. The planks of the three ships had all rotted, and it was impossible to verify when they sank.
