Bengbu: Smuggled Sugar Being Detained 91

In the midst of smuggling rumors, tax-evading sugar from North China has been flowing into Bengbu. Recently, customs anti-smuggling officers have been stationed in Bengbu to investigate. Many sugar vendors have transferred to various counties and towns in northern Anhui to sell it. A batch of smuggled sugar, totaling 240 bags, was transported from the Bengbu river by sailboat to Zhengyangguan for sale. When the ship was berthed in the river outside the west gate of the town, it was learned by the district office. The official Zhu Liangfu and the chief of the Changhuai Aquatic Public Security Bureau went to inspect it. The boatman Zhang Wanbei, the escort Ge Guangjiang, Cai Qingfu, and Li Xihe were arrested, and the smuggled sugar was also found. According to the boatman, it was transported by Bengbu Lixing Exchange and two companies, totaling 240 bags, of which 86 bags had been sold, leaving 154 bags. Official Zhu took all three escorts to the office for detention, and at the same time strictly pursued the sugar that had been sold and telegraphed the special commissioner's office for instructions.

The Past Two Years of Jiangsu's Anti-Smoking Campaign "Part Two" 92

— Yu Jingtang

5. Smokers Self-Reporting and General Reporting of Opium Addicts

During the general registration period in this province, many smokers were genuinely poor and unable to obtain licenses, leading to evasion of registration. If they were all arrested and prosecuted, it would be truly pitiful. Therefore, in January of the 24th year [of the Republic], approval was obtained to conduct a smoker self-reporting initiative. Unregistered smokers were allowed to self-report to the relevant government offices before the implementation of the Jiangsu Province Interim Regulations for Punishing Opium Prohibition Offenses. They would be sent to addiction treatment centers for free treatment and exempted from criminal penalties to show leniency and caution in imprisonment. According to statistics, as of the day before the aforementioned regulations came into effect (March 31, 1935), a total of 9,244 smokers had self-reported in various counties. All of them had been treated and discharged from the centers. Subsequently, in February of the 25th year, to thoroughly eliminate opium addiction, after the new smoker registration was completed, a general reporting of opium addicts was conducted. Using the Baojia system, all levels of self-government personnel and land and water public security personnel in the province were ordered to mobilize fully, supervising at each level, and setting a deadline to complete the task. At the same time, special commissioners of administrative supervision and county magistrates in each district were instructed to personally supervise the work in their respective areas. The provincial government also dispatched 31 personnel to supervise and guide the work in various counties. In total, from February 16th of the 25th year to March 18th, 20,058 opium addicts were reported.

6. Prohibition of Planting Poppies and Suppression of Private Trafficking and Smoking

This province was designated as an absolutely prohibited planting area. In the winter of the 23rd year of the Republic, strict orders were issued to various opium merchants and county governments to forcibly eradicate poppy plants. Provincial security teams were also dispatched to assist in the process. Therefore, during the poppy seedling emergence period in the spring of the 24th year, personnel were repeatedly dispatched for overt and covert inspections, and it was reported that the plants had been almost entirely eradicated. This spring, personnel were again dispatched to various areas for thorough inspections. The results showed that due to the dedicated investigations and prohibitions by personnel at all levels over the past two years, no roots or plants were found in remote villages, high mountains, deep forests, or areas bordering neighboring provinces. The complete elimination of poisonous plants in the province can be declared.

The current opium prohibition method in this province adopts a phased elimination approach. Within the statutory time limit, registered smokers and approved opium paste shops and smoking parlors are allowed to operate and smoke legally. However, some unscrupulous individuals still defy the law and engage in private trafficking and smoking, undermining the progress of the prohibition policy. Therefore, strict measures have been repeatedly formulated and earnestly implemented for anti-smuggling work. On one hand, to carefully select anti-smuggling personnel, 80 investigators were recruited in [month missing], 23rd year. A training class for investigators was established, and after four months of rigorous training, they were assigned to various counties to carry out investigative work. In January of the 24th year, a major investigation training group was established, selecting several police dogs to assist in various search skills for hidden opium, including shallow hiding, deep hiding, mobile hiding, high hiding, buried hiding, and water hiding, to supplement the work of investigators. In total, from August of the 23rd year to April of the 25th year, a total of 19,398 opium-related cases were cracked by various counties independently, with the assistance of provincial investigators and search dogs.

7. Opium Prohibition Funding

In September of last year, the Department of Civil Affairs was ordered to take over the administration of opium prohibition. Due to changes in the organizational system, the opium prohibition funding budget established by the former Provincial Opium Prohibition Committee was no longer fully applicable. Therefore, considering the actual situation, a new overall budget for revenue and expenditure at the end of the 24th year was recompiled and submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval. The total annual revenue was estimated to be 1,132,672 yuan, and the monthly expenditure was estimated to be 100,938.50 yuan. Calculating for ten months this year, the total expenditure would be 1,093,385 yuan, which is still within the revenue limit. As for the procedures for receiving and disbursing opium prohibition funds, the Department of Civil Affairs, together with the Department of Finance and the Provincial Opium Prohibition Committee, formulated measures for handling opium prohibition funds and procedures for handling opium prohibition funds in various counties, in accordance with the province's current regulations for collecting and remitting provincial and county taxes and accounting regulations. In total, as of April 30th of this year, the total revenue from license fees was 936,725.31 yuan, and the total expenditure was 662,958.12 yuan. The actual surplus after offsetting revenue and expenditure was 273,767.19 yuan. However, because the year has not yet ended, only the actual amounts received and disbursed have been statistically analyzed. The various amounts that should have been collected or disbursed in May and June have not yet been included. A precise final account will be compiled at the end of the year.

Conclusion

The phased opium prohibition in this province, with registration and licensing, treatment, persuasion, search and re-examination, and livelihood assistance as the basic tasks of implementation control, aims to gradually achieve the goal of phased elimination. It has been implemented for two years now. The progress of the handling has been recalled above. Fortunately, personnel at all levels handling opium prohibition and local people have been able to promote it uniformly, so that the effectiveness has gradually become apparent. However, according to the current regulations, the period for treatment and the end of prohibition is only two years and four months away (the treatment year in this province began on October 1 of the 23rd year and is limited to four years, ending on September 30 of the 27th year). Given the large number of smokers in this province, the complexity of the local situation, and the shortage of opium prohibition funds, we must work even harder in the future to complete it as scheduled. So, what is the direction of our future efforts? The answer is: 1. Continue with the established policy and actively carry out smoker treatment, ensuring that registered smokers in various counties are effectively treated in batches according to their age and smoking volume, and in consideration of the capacity of the addiction treatment centers. 2. Conduct a general inspection of opium addicts to achieve the goal of thorough elimination. 3. Expand the facilities of the addiction treatment centers and strive to improve addiction treatment techniques and administrative management matters, so that smokers are happy to receive treatment and embark on a new path. 4. Establish organizations such as smoker vocational training factories, so that treated smokers have skills to make a living, increasing social production power. Other aspects, such as controlling opium paste shops and smoking parlors, managing smokers, and conducting spot checks and re-examinations, should continue to be actively carried out based on established policies, so as to eliminate abuses and create a clean atmosphere. We hope that local enthusiastic people will continue to assist in promoting this cause with their past sincerity, so that the opium prohibition policy in this province can be seen to succeed early. This is what I sincerely pray for. (End)

June 3rd Commemoration Meeting (Photographed by Guobi Art Society)

Chairman's Speech

After the ceremony, Chairman Lu Jingshi delivered the opening speech, stating that, "Fellow compatriots, today is the 'June 3rd' Opium Prohibition Memorial Meeting held by representatives from all sectors of Shanghai. The significance of today's commemoration is to make the public aware of the history of 'June 3rd.' This historical memorial day can make us have a deep sense of memorial value, because this is the beginning of the imperialists' invasion of us, that is, the beginning of the initial establishment of unequal treaties. The opium disaster in the country is so severe. Ninety-seven years ago today, Mr. Lin Zexu, in view of the scourge of opium, implemented opium prohibition. At that time, due to the lack of a strong group and the government's lack of determination, a war was started with the British and failed, but it was glorious. Now the people are extremely poor. The reason lies in opium. If this kind of drug is not eliminated, there is no way to revive the nation. Therefore, the government has made a great determination to ban opium and drugs. The results in the past year have been very good. The international community also knows that we are strictly banning opium and drugs. The cooperation between the government and the people is very admirable. We can only continue to work hard to relieve the national crisis and rely on our own efforts. We can only thoroughly eliminate drugs and break away from drugs."

Mr. Wang's Report

After the Chairman's speech, Mr. Wang Xiaolai reported on the opium prohibition situation in the city, stating that, "Brothers, on behalf of the Opium Prohibition Association, I report on the general situation of opium prohibition in Shanghai. Since April of the 23rd year, the Nanchang Headquarters reorganized the Hubei Special Tax Office into the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office, handling opium prohibition affairs in ten provinces. Liu was in charge of military law and decided on a two-year drug prohibition and six-year opium plan, successively promulgating various opium prohibition laws to thoroughly ban opium. The city established the Opium Prohibition Committee in July of the 24th year, hiring Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Yan Fuqing, Wang Yiting, Wang Boqi, Yu Zuoting, and Yu Qiaqing as members, responsible for supervising the progress and improvement of opium prohibition. Smoker registration began in July of the 24th year. The Public Security Bureau specially set up a smoker registration section, which handled registrations until the end of December, registering a total of 30,844 smokers, including 11,838 who obtained ordinary five-yuan licenses and 17,995 who obtained six-jiao poor people's licenses. Regarding the situation of addiction treatment, (A) a temporary addiction treatment center was established in Longhua. From June of the 23rd year to June of the 24th year, 2,211 people were forcibly treated and 1,173 people voluntarily sought treatment. From July to April of the 25th year, there were a total of 1,712 people, for a total of 4,096 people. (B) The Huinan Addiction Treatment Hospital was established (at Santai Pier in Nanshi), with a total of 2,445 men and women treated. (C) The Hubai Addiction Treatment Hospital was established (on Tiantong'an Road in Zhabei). From May of the 24th year to May of the 25th year, a total of 3,315 men and women were treated. (D) The criminal addiction treatment hospital was established. From September of the 24th year to April of the 25th year, a total of 935 men and women were treated. (E) Other designated addiction treatment hospitals, from July to December of the 24th year, reported a total of 61 men and women treated. In total, 10,852 men and women have been treated for opium addiction. Although there are no statistics on those who voluntarily quit opium addiction, the number must be considerable. Regarding license handling, addiction treatment licenses are checked every six months. It is hoped that smokers with licenses will go to the Public Security Bureau to exchange for new licenses when they expire to avoid losing protection. A standard for phased treatment has been determined, based on age and smoking volume, with the first year for those under 30 years old, the second year for those under 40 years old, the third year for those under 50 years old, the fourth year for those under 60 years old, and the fifth year for those over 60 years old. [missing] The Smoker Registration Examination, Chairman Chiang issued an order in February of this year to conduct a reporting of smoker registration and promulgated 14 articles for the method of reporting smokers. After receiving the order, the city cooperated with reporting commissioner Mr. Ma Liang to handle it together. It has now begun. It is hoped that smokers in the city will not miss this last opportunity and quickly go to the Public Security Bureau to complete the registration. The above is a general overview of the opium prohibition work in the city over the past year. It is hoped that representatives from all sectors will continue to urge the government to cooperate with the government to thoroughly eliminate this enemy of our nation that has been harming us for more than a hundred years. This is not only a blessing for the city but also a blessing for China. After the report was completed, I had a little feeling, that is, opium drugs must be banned, and cigarettes are not noticed by ordinary people, but in fact, the annual consumption loss is also considerable. The annual leakage is 80 million. I have been breaking away from cigarettes for 28 years. I hope that those who [missing] quit at any time."

Generally speaking, the Opium War has had a great impact on our country. At that time, Qing Qian only knew to seek safety in the north and did not hesitate to compromise and seek surplus, signing the Treaty of Nanjing, opening Shanghai, Ningbo, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Guangzhou, and five ports as trading ports, and withdrawing Mr. Lin to reconcile. If the Qing court was the backing, then Mr. Lin's opium prohibition success can be expected. I sincerely hope that compatriots who are addicted to opium will no longer wait and see and abandon themselves. You must know that those who can love their own bodies are also loving the country. If you want to release the shackles of national treaties, you must first release the individual from the shackles of hobbies. Self-strength and strong country, is what I hope for the self-awareness of compatriots."

Japan Increases Troops in North China and Engages in Smuggling; Chamber of Commerce Cables Government Requesting Negotiations; Customs Prevents Smuggling on Roads; Various Industries Notify Members to Take Precautions 98

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Jiang Telegram

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Executive Yuan and Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating: "To the Honorable Executive Yuan and Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Nanjing: Japan's increasing of troops in North China, as well as preventing customs from suppressing smuggling, leading to increasingly rampant smuggling, is a major event that hinders our country's sovereignty and undermines the lifeline of our finances. Repeated negotiations have failed to yield results. The government should urgently adopt a firm and determined spirit and consistently maintain its position. Regarding Japan's increasing of troops in North China, it is using the Boxer Protocol and the protection of overseas Chinese as excuses. However, Article 9 of the Boxer Protocol states that the purpose of stationing troops is to protect the Beijing-to-Sea passage. In essence, it is for the safety of the embassies, not for the purpose of protecting overseas Chinese. Therefore, the protocol stipulates that the troop stationing locations are all along the Beijing-Shenyang Railway line and are not specifically focused on treaty ports with overseas Chinese. Now, the Beijing-to-Sea passage is not in danger of obstruction. Increasing troops for protection is not necessary in fact. Moreover, the current troop stationing location of Fengtai originally belonged to China's responsibility. According to Article 1 of past treaties, it was originally China's responsibility. According to past treaties, there has never been a provision for self-stationing of troops for protection. Even considering the previous situation in the three northeastern provinces, troop deployment was limited to the South Manchurian Railway protection zone and not in every treaty port with overseas Chinese. Yanji Prefecture is a precedent. If we take today's North China as an example, with tens of thousands of Japanese overseas Chinese, it would require stationing a brigade to protect them. At that time, Yanji Prefecture had one to two hundred thousand Korean overseas Chinese under Japanese nationality. Wouldn't that require stationing several divisions to protect them? A comparison clearly demonstrates the lack of a basis for their argument. As for customs suppressing smuggling, according to Article 18 of the Sino-Japanese Trade Treaty, China has the right to devise and implement measures to prevent smuggling in all treaty ports. The Tanggu Truce Agreement signed by military officers of both countries cannot affect the trade treaty signed by the two governments. Moreover, customs police belong to the customs and are completely different from the military system. They cannot be considered part of the military and subject to the truce agreement. We earnestly request the government to exert all efforts in negotiation based on international law and past treaties to safeguard the nation's lifeline. This is in the public interest. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully appeals, Jiang."

Ministry of Finance Reply Telegram

The Ministry of Finance telegrammed the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, stating: "The government has promulgated measures to prevent road transport smuggling, interim regulations for punishing tax evasion, and interim regulations for inspecting the sale of imported goods, all to stop smuggling. Strict enforcement has been ordered. Having read the chamber's telegram and attached copies, the submitted points align with the government's intentions. If industries and businesses can uphold their patriotic sincerity and recognize the pain of tax revenue loss, smuggled goods will naturally disappear. This will not only benefit the country through tax revenue but also protect industries and businesses themselves. Please communicate this immediately to relevant parties for their information."

Jianghai Customs Proclamation

Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Hai'an and Customs Commissioner Ba Runsen jointly issued Proclamation No. 1519, stating: "It has been verified that the Executive Yuan has approved measures to prevent road transport smuggling, which have been ordered to be implemented. The General Inspectorate for Preventing Road Transport Smuggling of the Customs has also issued Proclamation No. 1. According to the regulations in the aforementioned measures, all foreign goods transported by rail must have a tax-paid certificate issued by the customs. Otherwise, the railway bureau will refuse to transport them. It is hereby determined that from June 3 of this year, merchants transporting the foreign goods listed in the attached table from this port to other places via rail shall, one day before loading the goods, obtain a "Tax Payment Certificate Application Form" from this customs office, fill it out according to the prescribed format, and submit it along with all the original import tax documents for the goods. After verifying that it matches the original import declaration, the tax payment certificate will be issued free of charge. This certificate can then be presented to the customs inspection offices at various Shanghai stations of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways or at the Wuxi station for verification. After the verification office confirms that the goods and documents match, it will sign and stamp the certificate. The merchant can then submit the certificate along with the railway freight car to the railway for consignment. After this proclamation, if any of the foreign goods listed in the attached table are transported by rail without this certificate, they may be seized by the customs officers stationed at the arrival station. The goods listed in the attached table may be subject to change depending on the circumstances. This proclamation is hereby issued for the information of all merchants. Attached is a list of foreign goods transported by road that require verification of the customs tax payment certificate: artificial silk, alcohol, alcoholic beverages, whiskey, brandy, champagne, gin, Japanese sake, various liqueurs, aniline dyes, dry batteries, rubber boots, canned food, cigarette paper, dried scallops, cosmetics and perfumes, electrical materials, needles, kerosene, diesel, various piece goods, rubber tires, rubber shoes, various dried seafood products, and sugar products."

Forwarding Industry Notice

The Shanghai Forwarding Industry Guild, in order to assist the government in preventing smuggling, convened an emergency standing committee meeting on the first day of this month. Standing committee members Zhou Renqing, Zheng Bochang, Ying Zihua, and Li Mulian, among others, attended. Li Mulian chaired the meeting. It was resolved that, from this day forward, all forwarding companies should only accept foreign goods entrusted by merchants and firms with customs permits; otherwise, they should refuse to transport them. The emergency notice issued by the guild is recorded below: (Notice 1) Greetings: Recently, the government has been rigorously cracking down on smuggling and has established special articles to actively handle it. All of our fellow industry members, being in the position of transportation, should strictly prevent any mingling of goods to assist the government. Therefore, at 2 PM on the first day of this month, we held a temporary emergency standing committee meeting, where it was decided that, from this day forward, any foreign goods entrusted by merchants and firms without a customs permit should be refused for transportation. Please do not attempt to do so, lest you cause trouble for yourselves. In addition to publishing this in the newspaper, we specially issue this solemn notice. Please pay special attention to it. Sincerely, Shanghai Forwarding Industry Guild. (Notice 2) Greetings: Recently, the government has been rigorously cracking down on smuggling and has established special articles to actively handle it. All merchants and firms, as well as fellow industry members, should carefully take precautions and comply. Therefore, we convened a temporary emergency standing committee meeting on the first day of this month, where it was decided that, from this day forward, any foreign goods entrusted by merchants, firms, etc., without the original customs permit should be refused for transportation. If the permit does not match the goods, the merchants themselves will be responsible. In addition to notifying fellow industry members in the city, we are publishing this statement in the newspaper again. Please pay special attention to it. We issue this notice for your information.

Zhejiang Province Agrees to Release 60% of Confiscated Silk Cocoons for Export; Remaining 40% Awaits Legal Disposition; Manufacturers Hope for Prompt Release to Avoid Disputes 99

Regarding the Zhejiang Silk Control Committee's confiscation of silk cocoons from silk manufacturers and cocoon merchants within the province whose cocoon pulling prices were below the central price for export, the Shanghai Silk Manufacturers Guild presented its reasons and telegraphed requesting release. A reporter from Xin Sheng News visited Mr. Shen Huachen, chairman of the Silk Industry Guild, yesterday and received detailed information, which is recorded below.

Release 60% First

Regarding the Zhejiang Provincial Government's confiscation of spring cocoons obtained by silk manufacturers and silk merchants within the province whose cocoon prices were below the central price for export, this guild has telegraphed the Silk Control Committee requesting prompt release. Based on its observation, the matter will not escalate because the low price of Chinese silk in European and American markets and the inferior quality of this year's cocoons compared to last year are factual issues. The Zhejiang Silk Control Committee is also very clear about this. According to reports from members in Hangzhou via long-distance telephone, Zhejiang Province has agreed to release 60% of the confiscated spring cocoons for export first, while the remaining 40% will await legal disposition. Therefore, it is expected that a peaceful resolution will be reached soon.

Significant Impact

If this matter is not resolved quickly, serious problems will inevitably arise. This year, manufacturers received loans from the financial sector to purchase cocoons, using the purchased cocoons as collateral. If the collateral is confiscated, disputes will inevitably arise. Manufacturers have already sold silk to foreign firms, but they may not be able to pay on time because the previously sold silk prices were higher than current prices. Foreign firms will inevitably take the opportunity to cancel contracts. As for the current price of Chinese silk, B-grade standard silk is worth 570 national currency. The price of Chinese silk on May 20 when the cocoons were purchased was 640 yuan, a difference of 70 yuan.

Cholera Prevention Announcement 100

Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office Announcement No. 1: It is now June, and this year seems to be a "cholera year," with a possible epidemic. This office is issuing its first announcement. According to past experience, there is a periodic outbreak every three or four years. The personnel of this office's epidemic prevention team are experts from various health agencies in Beijing and Shanghai. They have worked hard to study the causes of this outbreak and seek appropriate prevention and control methods. Specifically studying weather factors, it seems that there is too much rainfall in general, but the table below shows that it is not too much.

Over the past 65 years, the average rainfall in this port from January to May has been 14.87 inches. Therefore, this year's rainfall is still below the average. Compared with the rainfall and rainy days in 1920 and 1922, the difference is very large. According to the opinions of health authorities such as Sir Keith, short rainfall is conducive to the spread of cholera. In 1923, the rainfall from January to May was 12.47 inches, and there were many cholera cases. However, last year's rainfall at the same time was 10.27, and there was no cholera outbreak. Therefore, in terms of rainfall, it seems difficult to predict that there is a possibility of an epidemic this year, but we must still pay attention and cooperate with health agencies to achieve preventive effects. Cholera is often a disease transmitted through water, but it is not limited to drinking water. Contaminated hands, unclean utensils, contaminated vegetables, fruits, cold drinks, and flies can all cause it. Therefore, all unheated foods and unreliable beverages should be avoided. Food preparers must wash their hands. Regarding the above matters, all homeowners and employers should be responsible for guiding servants and workers. During a cholera epidemic, the working class suffers the most. Various municipal authorities in Shanghai and the water company provide free water for the benefit of the poor. There are now 30 free water taps in the Public Concession, open at fixed times every day, and 91 in the French Concession. The poor can fetch water at fixed times. There are more than 50 places in Shanghai, so all poor people should no longer drink contaminated water. A new water plant has also been recently established in Pudong, and the poor in that area will also receive the same benefits in the future. However, among the poor, there must be those who live too far from the water facilities or do not have time to fetch water when the taps are open. Therefore, other water sources, such as wells and ponds, are also disinfected by health agencies. In the event of a cholera outbreak, thanks to this comprehensive protection, it is expected to reduce the spread and prevent it from expanding. Regarding cholera vaccination, it began on April 15 in the French Concession, May 1 in the Public Concession, and May 15 in Shanghai. This preventive method has gradually gained the trust of the public since 1930, and the number of recipients has increased every year. The number of vaccinations in the past six years is listed below.

It is hoped that the number this year can be increased. It is hoped that the residents of this metropolis can be vaccinated once a year, regardless of whether an epidemic is discovered in the future. Mobile vaccination vehicles and health sub-stations are distributed throughout the city so that residents can be vaccinated nearby. This vaccination is completely free. The educational propaganda carried out in streets, schools, factories, and other places has achieved considerable results, which can be used to awaken the public and make them aware of the importance of preventing cholera. Knowledgeable people should also do their best to help with this matter. This year, there are about eight hospitals in this port that can accommodate cholera patients, with a total of about 1,000 beds. The names of the hospitals and the number of beds are listed on the left.

After cholera occurs, the patient should be sent to a suitable hospital for treatment immediately. This should not be ignored. A slight delay can endanger their life.

More Than 40 Industries' Workers Demand Restoration of Organizations; Assist Government in Reporting Smuggling; Merchants Tend to Seek Profits, So It is Difficult to Guarantee They Will Not Traffic Smuggled Goods; Workers Are Closely Related to Business and Can Report at Any Time 101

Workers in more than 40 industries, including the local produce, pharmaceutical, sauce, pharmacy, Chinese and foreign cloth, dyeing, rice, ginseng, food, cosmetics, department store, etc., in order to assist the government in reporting smuggling and unified command, specially jointly submitted a request to the central government to restore the workers' union organization. The original submission is recorded as follows: "We are submitting this to request approval to restore the workers' organization to assist the government in effectively reporting smuggling. We respectfully observe that since our workers' organizations were deemed incompatible with current laws in 1930 and should not exist, the status of workers has been transferred to members of the industry guild. For several years, how many workers have been able to participate in the industry guild? All authority is in the hands of the capitalists. The worker's position has been abandoned by the industry and abandoned by society. We are all citizens, but is this fair? Looking back to the time when our workers had organizational structures, their history of promoting government policies and assisting in national construction was quite effective in the progress of the revolution. Recently, Japanese ruffians in North China have been smuggling and evading taxes, which has become increasingly serious. Our central government, in order to protect tax revenue and maintain industry, has strictly revised the interim regulations on punishing tax evasion to curb private sales. This is an urgent plan for the present. Merchants tend to seek profits, which is a common human sentiment. In the face of huge profits from smuggled goods, they are willing to violate the law and take risks, even to death. (Omission) Smuggled goods have gradually expanded from North China to other regions, rushing directly to the central ports along the Tianjin-Pukou and Peiping-Tianjin lines. Coastal ports, such as Shanghai and other places, will also be affected. Smuggled goods are like a sudden storm. In a few months, the loss of national tax revenue has reached more than 100 million yuan. The losses to industry and commerce affected by smuggled goods are several times that amount. If this continues, the national economy will inevitably be fundamentally shaken. We look to the future with deep fear. Our workers are part of the nation. At this time of national crisis, we will not stand idly by. Although our workers are hired by shopkeepers, they have a close relationship with business and no direct vested interests. Even if the business becomes rich, the workers will get nothing and merely satisfy the capitalists. Therefore, they can't earn any benefit from this. As smuggled goods become rampant, it is difficult to guarantee that unscrupulous merchants won't become involved. If capitalists traffic in smuggled goods, workers will see it with their own eyes and can hardly conceal it. We can assist the government in reporting smuggling without leaving anything out. In order to ensure the strictness of the reporting work and the speed of action, it is necessary to allow workers to restore organizational structures. The entire plan should be discussed and implemented by the organization. The effectiveness will be far better than the methods promulgated by the government. Therefore, we specially jointly and sincerely request your union (department) to promulgate separate regulations for workers as soon as possible so that they can organize according to law. We respectfully submit this to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department and the Central Party Department for National Training, awaiting orders."

General Manager of China Industrial Bank, Hu Mengjia, Passed Away Yesterday; Financial Circles Universally Mourn; Gong Xianzhou Presides Over Bank Affairs 102

Mr. Hu Mengjia, Director of the National Treasury Bureau of the Central Bank and General Manager of the China Industrial Bank, suffered from anemia due to overwork in early spring of this year. He sought medical treatment for several months, but his condition did not improve. On September 22, he moved into Fumin Hospital on North Sichuan Road for treatment, staying in room 17 on the fifth floor. After an X-ray examination by the hospital, no other symptoms were found, but his anemia worsened daily. This was reported in this newspaper. He underwent three blood transfusions, three injections of special saline solution, and five injections of cardiac stimulants, but the effect was minimal. His blood pressure and fever increased daily, causing his physical strength to decline. He once experienced urinary incontinence. Since May 28, his condition suddenly worsened again. Despite ineffective treatment, he passed away at 1:10 PM yesterday. His family notified the China Funeral Home on Haig Road to transport his remains to the funeral home by car and temporarily placed them in the West Hall. Surgery and embalming will be performed. The funeral will be held at 10 AM on June 5. Upon hearing the news, the financial circles in this port expressed their condolences and elected Qian Xinzhi and others to handle the funeral arrangements. Mr. Hu's name was Zuitong, and Mengjia was his courtesy name. He had five brothers. Hu was the eldest, 49 years old, the second named Cilang, the third named Shushao, and the fourth named Jiping, childhood name Shaoqing, all of whom are currently employed by the Central Communications and Shanghai Industrial Trust Society. He was originally from Yin County, Zhejiang Province. He graduated from the University of Birmingham in the United Kingdom with a master's degree in economics and was elected as a member of the Royal Economic Society of the United Kingdom. He returned to China in the first year of the Republic of China and was hired as a professor and dean at the Zhejiang Hangzhou College of Politics and Law and other schools. He entered the financial industry about eight years later, first serving as the deputy manager of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank and then as the deputy general manager of the head office of the Bank of Communications in Peiping. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the bank moved south, and Hu was appointed as the general manager of the head office, manager of the Shanghai branch, and was twice elected as a Chinese director of the Shanghai Public Concession Board of Directors. In addition to serving as Director of the National Treasury Bureau of the Central Bank and General Manager of the China Industrial Bank, he also served as a standing director of the Bank of Communications, director of the Shanghai Bankers' Association, director of the China Enterprise Bank, and supervisor of the Guohua Bank. He was honest and self-disciplined, eager to help others, and especially fond of charity work, so he did not accumulate much savings after his death. He is survived by five sons and six daughters. The eldest son is only 19 years old and is studying at Peicheng Girls' School. The youngest daughter is only six years old. His wife, Ms. Bi, is in her thirties. She once provided blood transfusions for Mr. Hu. His second daughter, named Yixin, is 18 years old and is also studying at Peicheng. The Board of Directors of the China Industrial Bank unanimously elected Chairman Gong Xianzhou and Standing Director Li Jizhi to go south to preside over the bank's affairs after learning of Mr. Hu's death. Mr. Gong and Mr. Li have both held important positions in the political world and are giants in the banking industry. The bank's business will surely thrive in the future. However, it is a great pity that Mr. Hu's knowledge made him one of the most talented people in China, but he has passed away.

Zhang Shizhao Emphatically Advocates that the Constitution Should Prioritize Facts; Never Mentioned Advocating Dictatorship; Absolutely No Memorial was Submitted; —The Truth About His Speech at Jiang's Banquet— 106

According to the New Sound News Agency, lawyer Zhang Shizhao recently went to Beijing for legal affairs and visited friends in the government. He attended a banquet hosted by President Jiang on May 26, where he made some remarks about the draft constitution. The content of these remarks was unknown to outsiders, leading to rumors in Beijing and Shanghai that Mr. Zhang advocated for presidential dictatorship and had submitted a ten-thousand-word memorial to President Jiang. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency visited Mr. Zhang at his residence yesterday, asking him to reveal the truth within the realm of possibility to dispel misunderstandings.

Discussing Ideals is Indeed a Mistake

Mr. Zhang said, "I am naturally frank and have nothing to hide. Before the draft constitution was announced, Mr. Wang Liangchou told me that the constitution was based on the people, and he hoped that legal scholars outside the party would provide fair criticism to arouse the interest of the people in the constitution. I replied that the constitution should be realistic, not ideal. Twenty years ago, we were fond of discussing the constitution based on personal ideals, which was indeed a mistake. I have not written political essays for many years, and due to my efforts to earn a living, I have not had time to study the political organization of the current National Government in detail. Since Mr. Wang asked me to criticize the constitution, I had to briefly examine the current political situation before writing to avoid being out of touch with reality."

Prioritizing Facts Over Ideals

"My speech in Beijing this time was generally along these lines. My words at President Jiang's banquet were also similar. I also cited the example of France, saying that after the French Revolution, the People's Party liked to create a constitution based on pure ideals, but its implementation often led to friction. As a result, the constitutional draft was repeatedly created and rejected, reaching twelve times. It was not until the final Third Republic that it accommodated reality, vigorously advocated simplicity, and announced the constitution of 1870, which stabilized the situation. For the past sixty or seventy years, France has been thriving. A constitution that prioritizes facts over ideals is the most appropriate example."

Absolutely No Memorial was Submitted

"The French have very high ideals, separating the creation of law from legislation. A constitution should be created by a constitutional body, meaning that the state precedes the constitution, and the government follows the state. Creating law means creating the law that precedes the state, while legislation means establishing the law by which the government is governed. The boundaries between these are very clear. However, the Third Republic's constitution even included a clause appointing General MacMahon as the first president for a seven-year term. This concerns the government's personnel matters, which is several levels below constitutional creation. Yet, the constitution emphasized it so prominently, disregarding its own rules. This shows that reality is compelling and can overthrow ideals. As for how well our country's draft constitution aligns with the current reality, I have not yet begun to study it and cannot make a judgment. However, I can confidently assert that the constitution should prioritize facts. The purpose of my speech at the time was roughly this. As for the rumors that I advocated dictatorship, I never mentioned it. Absolutely no memorial was submitted." The reporter found Mr. Zhang's words quite frank and recorded them as above, which can also be said to be beneficial to the current state of politics.

The Chinese General Federation of Industry and Labor held an executive committee meeting yesterday at 4 PM. Ministry of Railways Orders All Railway Bureaus to Prioritize the Use of Domestic Electrical Appliances 110

The Ministry of Railways, in order to promote domestic electrical appliances, issued an order to all railway bureaus and directly affiliated agencies, stating, "In accordance with the Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 3179 of May 21, 25th year of the Republic, the Shanghai Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Industry Association submitted on May 13, 25th year of the Republic, stating, 'Regarding the request to order all subordinate agencies and guide the people in various regions to purchase electrical appliances, all of which should be domestic goods. The manufacturing of domestic electric fans in our country has a history of 20 years. Because of their excellent quality and low prices, they are popular with people across the country and overseas Chinese compatriots. When the production of domestic electric fans was not high, the price of imported electric fans was several times higher than the current market price. As the production of domestic electric fans increased, imported products could not compete with them due to tariffs and transportation costs. In addition, the people's enthusiasm for using domestic goods has become more and more fervent. They deeply feel that domestic electric fans are exquisite and even surpass imported products. As a result, the sales of imported electric fans have greatly decreased. Last year, domestic electric fan factories such as Huasheng, Huatong, and China Yabuer, seeing that competition with foreign countries depended on the unity and cooperation of the industry, organized a joint sales office. Since its operation, it has gained the trust of the people. Unexpectedly, this has aroused the jealousy of foreign merchants, who have tried their best to destroy it. This year, they even imported electric fan parts separately, assembled them in Shanghai by hiring workers, seeking to reduce tariffs on the one hand and taking advantage of low wages on the other. They manufactured a small number of electric fans and deliberately lowered prices to disrupt the market. The annual production of domestic electric fans has recently reached more than 40,000 units, while foreign merchants only account for 4,000 to 5,000 units. Therefore, a price drop of 3 yuan per foreign unit would only result in a loss of more than 10,000 yuan. However, if domestic electric fans were to drop in price by 3 yuan as a result, the annual loss would be more than 100,000 yuan. The price fluctuations are very large. Now, foreign merchants are using this disruptive trick during the peak sales season, and domestic electric fan manufacturers can only bear the pain of cutting prices to avoid delaying time and unsold products. The magnitude of this loss is immeasurable. Furthermore, it is heard that foreign merchants have exhausted their strategies and will gradually increase their production each year, determined to completely occupy the domestic electric fan market. If this continues, how can domestic industries survive? Therefore, we request your council to order all subordinate agencies to use domestic electric fans from now on, and to issue an order to all provincial and municipal governments to encourage the people in various regions to purchase domestic goods when purchasing electrical appliances in the autumn of economic hardship, where national goods are dumped. This is a plea to maintain the lifeline of domestic goods factories and ensure that the nation's life is not reduced. We urgently appeal and humbly request your attention and prompt action.' Based on this, promoting domestic goods is the most important task at present. At this time of booming demand for electrical appliances, when the domestic electrical appliance manufacturing industry is still in its infancy, it should be especially promoted. In the future, all agencies and the people should prioritize the purchase of domestic products to maintain domestic goods and prevent leakage. In addition to issuing separate orders and instructions, we hereby order you to comply and instruct all subordinate agencies to comply as well. This order."

Zhang Binghui and Yan Wenkai Returned to Shanghai After Inspecting Japan; Talked About Japan's Admiration of Shanghai's Group Weddings; Many Aspects of Social Undertakings in Japan are Worth Learning From 112

Zhang Binghui, the chief of the fourth section of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and Yan Wenkai, the chief clerk of the bureau, were dispatched to Japan to visit the World Wedding Expo and inspect social undertakings. They have now completed their tasks and returned to Shanghai by the Shanghai Maru the night before last. In addition to reporting to the mayor, they released a joint statement yesterday, saying, "We were ordered to go abroad to inspect social undertakings in Japan and visit the World Wedding Expo. Due to the short duration of the trip, we were unable to study in detail. However, based on what we have seen and heard, we feel that social undertakings in Japan can develop evenly. Furthermore, due to the clarity of social surveys, the social undertakings that are undertaken are increased or decreased at any time according to the actual needs of society. For example, the public cafeterias run by the Tokyo Metropolitan Government have achieved great success, and more and more people are following suit. There is a proposal to reduce them this year. If childcare centers have not yet met the needs of society, there are plans to increase them. Other relief undertakings, although not seen as very developed, can concentrate their undertakings and unify their management policies, which increases efficiency and does not waste resources. It is necessary to learn from and improve the charitable undertakings in our city. Cooperative undertakings in Japan are called 'associations.' We visited the Tokyo Central Industrial Association and warehouse, which are large in scale. Their business provides loans to farmers and small businesses, which is a credit cooperative in nature and has been very successful. The anti-production movement of farmers' banks and middle-level merchants in various places shows a glimpse of the development of this type of association. As for consumer cooperation, there is no success to speak of other than family consumption associations in cities. As for the Japanese grain warehouses, which are world-famous, our city is currently planning to build warehouses. Therefore, we visited the largest rice grain bureau warehouse in Tokyo. The completeness of the equipment, the abundance of storage, and the rationality of the architecture are sufficient for us to emulate. The World Wedding Expo was held in Osaka, at Tsurumi Ryokuchi Park. Although the scale is not very large, it has collected wedding materials from around the world and has considerable views. In particular, the evolution of Japanese weddings is displayed using giant models, with lifelike expressions, which is very characteristic. Looking at the evolution of weddings around the world, they mostly came from coercion, buying and selling, and matchmaking. Recently, it has evolved to mutual love between the two sexes. Weddings have evolved from simple to complex, and now they are tired of complexity and tend to be simple. As personnel are becoming more and more complex, weddings have to become easier. The materials for group weddings collected from our city were all displayed in it. According to the person in charge of the association, many people from various countries who came to visit praised it and thought it could be used as a reference for the evolution of modern weddings. Wedding waste in Japan is comparable to that in our country. Therefore, they are particularly interested in group weddings and have the idea of imitating them. We met many overseas Chinese in Japan who often inquired about group weddings. Some even specially bought photos and hung them on the wall, requesting to visit Shanghai to see a group wedding. We feel very happy about this. As for the large number of unemployed and beggars in various cities in Japan, the government has tried its best to control them, so it is not easy to detect. We have two deep impressions during our trip to Japan: First, the Japanese people generally possess four spirits: diligence, hard work, frugality, and cleanliness. This is true even for government officials. Diligence can reveal subtleties, hard work can establish fate, frugality can know hardship, and cleanliness can embrace life. With these four paths, nothing cannot be advanced. This is the root cause of Japan's wealth and power. Second, education is universal. For matters that are not easy for the government to construct, they can all clearly identify their goals and sacrifice their individuals. The government uses its great power to complete construction. Unlike our country, where doing something often involves many constraints, leading to changes in the original plan, and the results are naturally difficult to see. If our country wants to become rich and strong, the above two points are especially important to study and implement." In addition, Japan pays the most attention to children's welfare undertakings. Children's playgrounds can be seen everywhere. Large stores in cities also have children's playgrounds on the roofs. The prices of children's books and all supplies are set low to make them easy to buy. They also pay great attention to child care, which is also worth learning from in our city.

Bandit Xu Renhe; Identified Among the Crowd by Witnesses; Definitely the Humaiyi Hotel Robbery 115

On the morning of the 20th of last month, at 1 AM, two bandits armed with weapons broke into the Humin Humaiyi Hotel at No. 393, Maybach Road, and robbed them of 8 yuan in legal tender. They shot and killed the hotel worker Liu Zifu and wounded Fan Tianfu with bullets. The case was already investigated by the New Zha Police Station and Chinese Detective Chief Hua Guo, who arrested the suspects: Hua Jinsen, the former platoon leader of the Security Regiment; Xia Jinliang; Xu Renhe; and six detectives from the Public Security Bureau: Zhang Zuoxian, Zheng Bucai, and Wang Yucai. They were sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. The details have been reported in this newspaper. This morning, the translator and judge from the Criminal Division 8 continued the interrogation. According to Zhang Tianyin, the lawyer for the police station, the police station is prosecuting Hua Jinsen and the other six defendants not only for selling military firearms and ammunition in violation of Article 187 of the Criminal Law, as they were found to possess a Ning brand pistol and eight bullets, but also for Xu Renhe for the crime of robbery and murder in violation of Article 332 of the Criminal Law. Because the case is being adjourned, the victim Fan Tianfu pointed out that Xu Renhe was at the scene robbing money. Also, the owner of the Humaiyi Hotel, Xu Yugui, also pointed out that Xu Renhe was holding a gun at the scene. Therefore, in order to clarify the facts of the case, it is requested that it be postponed again. Furthermore, according to the West Detective Chief Erkosi, he reported that he had mixed the defendant Xu Renhe among nine prisoners and asked the witnesses to identify him in the police station. Fan Tianfu, Xu Yunqiu, and another hotel worker, Hu Huanquan, identified him separately. Furthermore, according to Fan Tianfu, he is 60 years old and from Yangzhou. He runs a noodle shop. On the night of the robbery, two bandits broke into the shop. One bandit held a gun at the door, and the other bandit went inside to rob. The defendant Xu Renhe was the robber. The other bandit holding the gun was attacked by the hotel worker Liu Zifu, who was then shot and killed, and my left leg was wounded in two places. My injuries have not fully healed. Furthermore, according to Xu Yugui, I only saw the back of one bandit holding a gun, and it seemed to be the same height as Xu Renhe. When Xu Renhe was questioned, he flatly denied any involvement in the robbery and murder case. Judge Tan briefly questioned the other defendants and ordered them to be detained for further interrogation at a later date.

Accused of Adultery and Abandonment; Yang Zhongfen Still Fails to Appear; Claiming to Have Gone to Xiamen on Official Business 116

Liu Huizhen, a woman from Suzhou who lives at No. 58, Xinxiude Lane, Baike Road, is 22 years old. In December of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], when Liu was a prostitute in the brothel opened by her adoptive mother, Chen Laoliu, on Broadway Road, she was seduced by Yang Zhongfen, the current deputy director of the Central South Bank. At the time, Yang falsely claimed that he had no wife and was willing to marry Liu. They began to rent a house and live together, and their love was deep. On August 18 of last year, she gave birth to a son named Ali. Until the end of the year, Liu found out that Yang had a wife. She negotiated with him, but Yang immediately changed his mind. Not only did he cut off all daily expenses, but he also treated her like a stranger and never visited her. Liu hired lawyer Feng Buqing to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Yang Zhongfen of adultery and abandonment, requesting that he be punished according to the law, and also filed a civil lawsuit, requesting that he be ordered to pay living expenses and educational fees for the child, totaling 20,000 yuan in national currency. The case has been tried twice by the court, but because Yang Zhongfen failed to appear, the case was adjourned. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi continued the hearing in Criminal Division 3. The plaintiff, Liu Huizhen, arrived in court with her two-year-old son, Ali (but the defendant, Yang Zhongfen, did not arrive, and his lawyer appeared on his behalf, stating that Yang had been ordered by the chairman of the Central South Bank to go to Xiamen on official business, so he could not make it today and requested another adjournment. He would be responsible for bringing Yang to court next time). Judge Jiang adjourned the case to be heard again on the afternoon of the 15th of this month.

Muslim Association Celebrates the Prophet's Birthday: Grand Meeting Held in Qinglian Street, City, Yesterday Morning; Attended by Over Four Thousand Local Guests and Over One Hundred Foreign Guests 117

Yesterday (June 3rd) was the twelfth day of March in the 1355th year of the Islamic calendar, the birthday of the most holy Prophet Muhammad of Islam. The Shanghai Muslim Association specially led the city's Muslims in holding a grand commemorative meeting. It was broadcasted by the China-West Wireless Radio Station, with lectures given for three days, from 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM. Additionally, 200,000 leaflets were distributed by airplanes, and ten propaganda teams were organized to distribute 120,000 booklets in three series, and 100,000 copies of religious doctrine leaflets were distributed in five districts—east, west, south, north, and center—throughout the city. The details of the grand meeting are recorded as follows:

Venue Arrangement

The venue was the auditorium of the Chinese Islamic Studies Association. Outside the door, a large archway made of pine and cypress was erected, with the words "Shanghai Muslim Association Celebrates the Prophet's Birthday Commemorative Meeting" written on white cloth. Inside the entrance was a rest area for those who signed in, as well as for the security guards. To the left was the office of the general director, and next to the auditorium on the left was a guest room for visiting guests. In the center of the auditorium were hung the Party and national flags and a large framed mirror presented by Mayor Wu Tiecheng, with the words "Sage of Arabia" inscribed in the middle. Because the association feared that the auditorium would be too small to accommodate everyone, a sound system was specially installed on the large playground next to the auditorium to broadcast the speeches.

Attending Guests

From around 9:00 AM, guests began to arrive one after another. By 10:00 AM, the venue was already overflowing. It is estimated that over four thousand local guests and over one hundred foreign guests attended the meeting, making it a grand occasion.

Chairman's Report

The presidium consisted of Li Zhibo, Li Yunsheng, Da Pusheng, Ha Decheng, Xie Ke, Ren Yonghu, and Ma Tianying. After the meeting was called to order with the ringing of a bell, Mr. Mai Jun'er A recited the scriptures, and then Mr. Li Zhibo reported that Islam is a religion of peace and that today they were celebrating the Prophet's birthday for the sake of peace.

Speeches (Summarized)

Da Pusheng gave a speech about the life of the Prophet, detailing the virtues of the Prophet's life. Following that, Mr. Ye Bin spoke, and Indian Islamic philosopher Mr. Syed Haji spoke about the true meaning of God sending prophets to preach. It is not only for Islam, but actually for people all over the world. A Muslim who believes in God, the scriptures, and the Prophet should also believe in other scriptures and prophets. Islam knows no racial, national, or religious boundaries. We must know that Islam is broad in meaning, not narrow. We should be friends with the world and treat each other as brothers. If all the people in the world believed in Islam, then everyone would be under the teachings of the Prophet, forming one body. All the conflicts in the world can be eliminated, and we can enjoy the happiness of lasting peace. Mr. Ezra, the editor of the Shanghai Jewish newspaper, spoke about how Islam and Judaism can be considered sister religions because they share the same origin and are close to each other. All the essence of Islam is also the essence of Judaism, and they share the responsibility of proclaiming belief in the one true God. The five most important tenets of Islam are: belief in the one true God, praying five times a day, giving alms, fasting, and pilgrimage to Mecca. The Prophet shouldered the important mission of proclaiming religious doctrines and persuading the Arabs and the people of the world to believe in the one true God. Many critics argue that the Prophet spread Islam with the sword, but this is not true. The Prophet never used the sword to proclaim the truth but led people to the right path with lofty ideals and morals. Is such a great religious figure as the Prophet not worthy of admiration and commemoration? Mr. Zhang Shouyong spoke about how the world can only achieve peace if it can achieve "selflessness." The Prophet was the sage who was best able to achieve "selflessness," so Islam can become a religion of peace. Mr. Thomas, a translator for the Shanghai Times, spoke about how, in the teachings of the Prophet, it can be seen that the Prophet attached great importance to peace. The Prophet instructed us to greet each other with "peace," wishing each other the peace and tranquility of God. The meaning of peace is not limited to the material and superficial, but the spiritual peace or tranquility is the deeper meaning of "peace." Mr. Du Di, a director of the Shanghai Zhejiang Road Mosque, spoke about how the Prophet, upon receiving God's revelation, first corrected his own body and mind, and then persuaded the people of Mecca and Medina, and finally spread the message to people of all countries. We should understand our position. First, we must be clean and firm in our beliefs, and then proclaim the truth to the world and persuade people to enter the right path, etc. After the speeches were completed, the meeting was adjourned.

Evening Dinner

Last night, mosques on Shanghai Zhejiang Road, Fuyou Road, Xiaoshadu, and Nanmen all held lectures on religious doctrines and dinners, celebrating until dawn.

Completion Yesterday

Mad Dog Bites Ox; Gecko Found in Cow's Brain 123

A farmer surnamed Ye from Jiuguoqiao in Minhang Town had a domestic ox. A few days ago, while grazing in the wild, it was suddenly bitten by a mad dog. Within a few days, the ox went mad and kicked pedestrians. The owner secretly sold it to a certain ox village in the north. When the owner sent someone to pull the ox, he was kicked down by the mad ox. The owner, seeing that the ox was seriously mad, invited many people to beat and hoe it together, and then killed the mad ox. A gecko (i.e., scorpion) was found curled up in the brain. Later, someone from the ox village dragged the cow into the river and disappeared.

Yang Ruigen and Sun Jia were each sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment and deprived of public rights for two years. Two Westerners' Interview About the Winner of the First Prize of the 22nd Aviation Lottery 126

The first prize number of the 22nd Aviation Highway Construction Lottery is 101564, which was jointly won by Francisco Garcia, a foreign employee of the Hong Kong Da Lai Shipping Company, and his friend Constantino Rodas. Last month, Garcia and Rodas came to Shanghai from Hong Kong by wheel to collect the prize money. A reporter from the Shin Shi News Agency heard the news and paid a special visit to the two gentlemen at their hotel to inquire about the circumstances of winning the prize, which was quite interesting. The details are recorded as follows:

Addicted to Buying Tickets, Won Four Prizes

Garcia was radiant and amiable, sucking on a light cigar and spitting out wisps of smoke, very satisfied. According to him, the aviation lottery has been drawn in the past, and its credibility is well-known. I am very addicted to buying lottery tickets. I buy several tickets every issue, or more than a dozen. My friend Rodas works at the Hong Kong Life Insurance Company and has the same addiction as me. He often contributes to buy with me. We often buy lottery tickets from the Shanghai National Government Aviation Lottery Office or the Dayun Company by mail. I have won six or seven small prizes, and I won four prizes once last year. I thought I was lucky, but I didn't expect the first prize of the 22nd issue to be won by me and Mr. Luo. It's really a surprise. From now on, we have a very good impression of the National Government Aviation Lottery.

Won the First Prize by Chance and Became a Wealthy Man

For the 22nd aviation ticket, Mr. Yu and Mr. Luo only bought one ticket together, which was still purchased by mail from Shanghai Dayun Company. When the lottery was drawn on May 8th, my friend happened to be going to the Philippines on business, and the tickets he bought were also taken away by Mr. Luo. At that time, the number of the tickets purchased was not recorded, so after the first prize was drawn, I was still unaware of who the wealthy man belonged to. It was not until a few days later that Mr. Luo sent a quick telegram from the Philippines that I suddenly realized that Mr. Yu and Mr. Luo had become wealthy men with 250,000 yuan. At that time, the joy was beyond words. From now on, we have an extremely good impression of the National Government Aviation Lottery.

The Circumstances of Winning the Prize Are Twisting and Interesting

According to Mr. Rodas, I am very interested in aviation lottery tickets. I had no intention of getting rich at first, but I didn't expect that in the 22nd aviation lottery, I actually won the first prize with Garcia, which was completely unexpected. When the lottery was drawn, Yu Shi Garcia and I won the first prize, which was completely unexpected. When the lottery was drawn, Yu Shi took a business trip to the Philippines. I was lonely and used browsing newspapers to help me pass the time. One morning, I read the newspaper and saw the news of the aviation ticket drawing and the first prize number. I suddenly remembered that I had bought a ticket, which was still hidden in my suitcase. Why not take it out and check it? After checking it, the number of the ticket I bought was exactly the same as the number of the first prize drawn. In my surprise, I still felt half-doubtful. It was not known whether the number published in the newspaper was wrong. Therefore, I sent a quick telegram to Shanghai from the wheel to inquire about the truth from the Dayun Company, and paid the return telegram fee in full, asking them to reply by telegram as soon as possible. When my wheel was docked at Philport, Dayun Company's reply telegram had arrived. Only then did I know that I had become rich. After that, I used champagne to congratulate the reporter and wish him good luck. Finally, the reporter asked what he would use the prize money for. It is said that he is quite willing to invest in China and support all construction projects.

Upon the Bed, Wang Jiyang Dies Suddenly; Investigation Clearly Indicates Death by Illness 127

Wang Jiyang, a native of Ningbo, aged fifty-seven, was the head mechanic at the Guanghua Petroleum Company. He resided in Jiangxinsha, Pudong. Recently, the Guanghua Company ceased operations, and the owed bonuses to employees and laborers, amounting to tens of thousands of gold, were delayed. Negotiations were unsuccessful. Wang was selected by his colleagues as a representative to resolve the matter through legal means. Yao took him by carriage to the Jì Hospital, but he died before receiving treatment. The hospital notified the French Concession police, who dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for autopsy. Meanwhile, Wang's wife, Wang Wangshi, was summoned for questioning. The next day, a report was made to the Second Special Court. Yang Binghua, a native of Hangzhou, aged thirty-three, residing at No. 21 Xinshou'an Lane, Min Ti Ni Yin Road, French Concession, formerly worked as an account keeper at the Gong Wu Stage theater on Avenue Edward VII. Yang Binghua stated that Wang Jin was competing for the position of account keeper at the Gong Wu Stage, and he (Yang) mediated a cooperation arrangement, with them voluntarily contributing a share of the payment each month for over a year. Yesterday, when going to settle accounts, a dispute and mutual assault occurred, and his (Yang's) lower body was also injured, requesting an examination. Liu Genshen stated that he stopped to watch at the Gong Wu Stage and was therefore considered an accomplice. Subsequently, both sides' lawyers requested that bail be allowed during the postponement. The court reviewed the statements and ruled for a postponed retrial. The defendants were allowed to provide a guarantor who would ensure their presence when summoned. After the court session, Yang immediately submitted a petition to the prosecutor's office requesting an injury examination.

Jiang Yanze Inheritance Lawsuit; Retrial Postponed Yesterday Due to Incomplete Witnesses 129

Jiang Yanze Pharmacy (also known as Jiang Family Pharmacy) outside Xiaonanmen is one of the famous pharmacies in Shanghai. The store has been inherited from ancestors to the present, managed by Jiang Lichuan of the eldest branch. All annual profits are shared by the descendants. Now, Jiang Lian (aged fifty-three) of the third branch, has retained lawyer Xu Xingti to file a lawsuit in the District Court, suing his older brother Jiang Lichuan for seizing jointly owned property and requesting its handover and division. The suit states that the eastern building at No. 44 Licang Bridge Street inside Xiaonanmen, consisting of a hall, wing rooms, and a building, a hall wing room building, and a rear Rongtang wing room building, as well as the hall and seven fen, three li, and six mao of wasteland, originally belonged to the plaintiff, the defendant, the late brother Qiubin, and the deceased younger brother Yuanyü. The defendant is maliciously seizing property, intending to swallow it all. The inheritance of Qiubin should be properly jointly managed, as evidenced by the single note written by the defendant when Qiubin passed away in the ninth year of the Republic. Before his death, the deceased younger brother Yuanyü adopted the plaintiff's son Zhu as his adopted son, and his inheritance should be inherited by the plaintiff's son. The defendant occupies all the houses alone, causing the plaintiff to rent elsewhere, and the rent should be reimbursed. Jiang Lichuan does not recognize the plaintiff's son as Yuanyü's adopted son regarding the inheritance issue. All family property, including the pharmacy, has been passed down from ancestors over two hundred years ago and cannot be divided. As for the plaintiff's residence, he himself did not want to live there and there was no intention of exclusive occupation, but all repair costs are borne by the defendant and should be shared. Yesterday, after Judge Jiang Dade summoned the parties, a retrial was ordered due to incomplete witnesses.
